style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-98"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-99" style="margin-right: 0.05em;">R</span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-100" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-101">c</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-102">t</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-103" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-104">σ</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-111">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" mathvariant="normal">r</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi>R</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>R</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi></mrow></msub><mo>+</mo><mi>σ</mi><msup><mi>ω</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div>where <i>R</i> denotes the gas constant, <i>T</i> signifies the temperature of the system, <i>A</i> represents the effective area, <i>n</i> corresponds to the electronic transfer number, <i>F</i> stands for the Faraday constant, <i>C</i> reflects the Na<sup>+</sup> concentration, and σ is associated with the Warburg factor. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref54" aria-label="reference 54">(54)</a> The linear relation between <i>Z</i>′ and ω<sup>–1/2</sup> at low frequencies is depicted (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c). The calculated σ value for HC-1100A is 327 Ω S<sup>–1/2</sup>, representing a lower value compared to that for HC-1100 (456 Ω S<sup>–1/2</sup>). Moreover, the smaller σ value is indicative of a higher <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>, implying enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the HC-1100A. Moreover, the <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> between HC-1100 and HC-1100A was further compared by the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) test (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d–f). The HC-1100A sample possessed superior Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics than HC-1100 across nearly all sodiation/desodiation potentials, demonstrating that the removal of in situ CaSe templates can effectively optimize the microstructure of the material, promote the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>, and improve the Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/asset/images/medium/am3c16484_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/asset/images/large/am3c16484_0005.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) EIS analyses and (b) fitting results of the EIS of different HC samples. (c) Relationship between <i>Z</i>′ and ω<sup>–1/2</sup> in the low frequency. (d) Voltage response during a single circulating current pulse. Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients of (e) sodiation and (f) desodiation processes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/asset/images/large/am3c16484_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c16484&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Since CaSe acts as in situ templates to construct hierarchical pore structures, the vacancy defects exposed to the edge locations after removing CaSe led to an increase of intrinsic defects in the as-obtained HCs. The density functional theory (DFT) calculations were performed to further reveal the effect of intrinsic defects on the Na-graphene. Three models were simulated (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a–c), where the edge positions of type 1 and type 2 show divacancy defects, and type 3 corresponds to single vacancy defects. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55 ref56'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55 ref56" aria-label="reference 55 and 56">(55,56)</a> For comparison, the ideal graphene was also modeled (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/suppl_file/am3c16484_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>). The adsorption behavior of Na atoms on carbon structures was simulated. The calculated adsorption energy (<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub>) of Na atoms on ideal graphene is 0.055 eV, which indicates a thermodynamically unfavorable interaction between ideal graphene and Na. Contrastively, the corresponding <i>E</i><sub>ads</sub> values of type 1, type 2, and type 3 were calculated to be −0.58, −0.71, and −0.51 eV, respectively. Moreover, the establishment of intrinsic defects can significantly enhance the interaction between Na and carbon layers, facilitating Na storage and increasing Na adsorption capacity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57 ref58'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref57 ref58" aria-label="reference 57 and 58">(57,58)</a> Additionally, in terms of Na adsorption, the model with divacancy defects outperforms the model with single vacancy defects. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>d–i shows top and side views, which intricately elucidate the variations in electron density of various defect models. It is noteworthy that all structures exhibit a net charge gain, indicating a charge shift from the adsorbed Na to the closest C atom. Particularly, vacancy defects tend to concentrate more charge density, implying strong Na–C interaction. In this case, the presence of the intrinsic defects promotes the adsorption of Na, thereby enhancing Na storage performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref57" aria-label="reference 57">(57)</a> Furthermore, structures featuring divacancy defects exhibit a more apparent accumulation tendency of charge density. Therefore, this underscores the positive influence of intrinsic factors on enhancing Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption behavior. Furthermore, to assess the impact of the <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> modification on the dynamics of Na transport, a possible pathway migration of Na was modeled, and the relative diffusion energy barriers were calculated, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>j,k. The outcomes illustrate a significant decrease in the diffusion barrier with an increase of <i>d</i><sub>002</sub>. A larger <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> will facilitate Na diffusion between interlayers, resulting in an improved rate capability of HCs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59 ref60'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref59 ref60" aria-label="reference 59 and 60">(59,60)</a> Based on the calculation outcomes, it can be concluded that dual-functionalized Ca with interlayer Ca<sup>2+</sup> to widen the <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> and in situ CaSe templates to create hierarchical pore structures and induce intrinsic defects can thermodynamically and dynamically facilitate Na<sup>+</sup> storage and transport, contributing to excellent sodium storage performance.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/asset/images/medium/am3c16484_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/asset/images/large/am3c16484_0006.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. DFT models for the adsorption of Na atoms onto carbon structures with (a, b) divacancy defects and (c) single vacancy defects. Bader charge transfer for Na atom adsorption on carbon structures, in which green and yellow regions are used to signify increased and decreased electron density: (d–f) Top view and (g–k) side view. The C and Na atoms are depicted as black and yellow spheres, respectively. (j) Diffusion path and (k) relative energy of HCs with different interlayer spacing.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/asset/images/large/am3c16484_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c16484&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i10">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, biomass-derived HCs with precisely regulated microcrystalline and porous structures were synthesized and showed improved sodiation kinetics, benefiting from the synergetic effect of dual-functional Ca. It is further demonstrated that Ca simultaneously acts as natural dopants to expand the interlayer spacing and as in situ CaSe templates to induce the formation of hierarchical pore structures. Moreover, DFT calculations reveal that the appropriate <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> and intrinsic defects induced by dual-functional Ca thermodynamically and dynamically favor reversible adsorption/desorption and insertion/extraction processes of Na<sup>+</sup>. With the synergistic effect of engineering in both microcrystalline and pore structures, HC-1100A delivers a notable reversible capacity of 350.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, along with an impressive rate ability (108.4 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>). This work provides a feasible method for achieving simultaneous regulation of microcrystalline structure and pore structure, which is instructive for the development of state-of-the-art carbon materials and the advancement of next-generation SIBs.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c16484?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c16484</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Experimental details; SEM images; TEM images; XPS spectra of HC-900, HC-1000, and HC-1200; additional EDS mapping of HC-1100 and HC-1100A; CV curves and charge/discharge profiles of HC-900, HC-1000, HC-1100, and HC-1200; CV scans; separation of the capacitive and diffusion-controlled charge contributions and normalized capacitive charge contribution of HC-900, HC-1000, and HC-1200; theoretical model of graphite adsorption of Na; structural parameters table of hard carbon materials; and comparison of electrochemical performance with different hard carbon materials reported (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/suppl_file/am3c16484_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c16484/suppl_file/am3c16484_si_001.pdf">am3c16484_si_001.pdf (903.33 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c16484" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Construct NiSe/NiO heterostructures on NiSe anode to induce fast kinetics for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yu; Zhang, Ripeng; Qian, Ji; Gong, Yuteng; Li, Huanyu; Wu, Chuan; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy Material Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">0044</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EMANCZ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is of great significance to design and innovate electrode materials with unique structures to effectively optimize the electrochem. properties of the secondary battery.  Herein, inspired by neuron networks, an ingenious synthesis is proposed to fabricate NiSe with multidimensional micro-nano structures, followed by in situ construction of NiSe/NiO heterostructures via a temporary calcination.  The major structure of bulk NiSe synthesized by the solvothermal method is 3-dimensional micron cluster spherical particles interwoven by uniform one-dimensional nanofibers.  Such structures possess the synergistic advantages of nano and micro materials.  After a temporary calcination in air, NiSe/NiO heterostructures should be formed in the bulk NiSe, which provides a built-in elec. field to enhance diffusion kinetics of sodium ions.  This special neural-like network and heterojunction structures ensure the excellent structural stability combined with rapid kinetics of the electrode, releasing 310.9 mAh g-1 reversible capacity after 2,000 cycles at 10 A g-1.  Furthermore, the electrochem. storage and ion transport mechanisms are elaborated by electrochem. anal. and theor. calcn. in more detail.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr5Ef3_abxXULVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5cCSc9HdpdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhvFOju73I&amp;md5=6db1c80be6a84dcac1fdbe5921e4fb53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D127%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D658-666%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DQ.%2BQ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BS.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BH.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BY.%2BFang%26author%3DX.%2BS.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BC.%2BBao%26title%3DRice%2BHusk-Derived%2BHard%2BCarbons%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2017.11.054&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2017.11.054&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rice husk-derived hard carbons as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qiaoqiao; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Liu, Yuhan; Fang, Yuyan; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">127</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">658-666</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn ever-increasing attention for scalable elec. energy storage owing to the inexhaustible sources and wide distribution of sodium.  However, to develop feasible anode materials still remains a great challenge for the practical application of SIBs.  Here, the authors report hard carbons derived from a plentiful and deserted biomass of rice husk through a facile acid treatment and subsequent pyrolysis.  The study illustrates that the electrochem. properties of the rice husk-derived hard carbons (RHHCs) are significantly influenced by the pyrolysis temp. because of the discrepancy in their microstructure.  The RHHC pyrolyzed at 1300° (RHHC-1300) shows the highest reversible capacity of 372 mAh/g and good cycling stability and rate performance due to its large interlayer distance and suitable oxygen content.  Also, full sodium-ion batteries are assembled to examine the application prospect using Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C and RHHC-1300 as cathode and anode materials, resp., delivering a high-energy d. of 185 Wh/kg and stable cycling performance.  This work could intensify the fundamental understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in biomass-derived hard carbons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7xLrD2OlEKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5cCSc9HdpdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVygsLnI&amp;md5=a6f544f14c93cd2145157d257e916707</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.34133/energymatadv.0050"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, J. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Initiating High-Voltage Multielectron Reactions in NASICON Cathodes for Aqueous Zinc/Sodium Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Mater.                 10.34133/energymatadv.0050</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D0050%26journal%3DEnergy%2BMater.%2BAdv.%26author%3DJ.%2BS.%2BYue%26author%3DS.%2BQ.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BJ.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BY.%2BLu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DR.%2BZhao%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26title%3DInitiating%2BHigh-Voltage%2BMultielectron%2BReactions%2Bin%2BNASICON%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BAqueous%2BZinc%252FSodium%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.34133%252Fenergymatadv.0050&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.34133%2Fenergymatadv.0050&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Initiating high-voltage multielectron reactions in NASICON cathodes for aqueous zinc/sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yue, Jiasheng; Li, Shuqiang; Chen, Shi; Yang, Jingjing; Lu, Xueying; Li, Yu; Zhao, Ran; Wu, Chuan; Bai, Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy Material Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">0050</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EMANCZ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium superionic conductor (NASICON) is a class of compds. with robust polyanionic frameworks and high thermal stability, which are regarded as prospective cathodes candidates for secondary batteries.  However, NASICON cathodes typically have low discharge plateaus and low practical capacities in aq. electrolytes.  Here, Na3V1.75Fe0.25(PO4)2F3 is investigated as a cathode material for the aq. zinc/sodium batteries.  While the addn. of F helps with the improvement of NASICON structural stability, the low-cost Fe substitution has a pos. impact on the capacity increment, reaction voltage increases, and cycling stability improvement.  Because the Fe3+ substitution could induce a change in the spin magnetic moments of the 3d orbitals of the VO4F2 and FeO4F2 octahedra, the 2-electron reaction of V is activated, which are V4+ /V3+ and V5+ /V4+ redox couples.  As a result, the novel Na3V1.75Fe0.25(PO4)2F3 cathode delivers a high operating voltage of 1.7 V, a high energy d. of 209 W·h·kg-1 and stable lifespan (83.5% capacity retention after 6,000 cycles at 1 A·g-1) in the aq. zinc/sodium batteries.  This research demonstrates the practicality of activating multielectron reactions to optimize the electrochem. properties of NASICON cathodes for aq. secondary batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4de0JZR0FQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_a3lD_XDaDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXitlOmtLzP&amp;md5=eff39681884103c23fb91894cc0f3822</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.34133/2021/9819521"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Voronina, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.                 10.1039/D1CS00948F</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D51%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D4484-4536%26journal%3DChem.%2BSoc.%2BRev.%26issue%3D11%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26title%3DEther-Based%2BElectrolytes%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD1CS00948F&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD1CS00948F&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ether-based electrolytes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ying; Wu, Feng; Li, Yu; Liu, Mingquan; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4484-4536</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be strong candidates for large-scale energy storage with the benefits of cost-effectiveness and sodium abundance.  Reliable electrolytes, as ionic conductors that regulate the electrochem. reaction behavior and the nature of the interface and electrode, are indispensable in the development of advanced SIBs with high Coulombic efficiency, stable cycling performance and high rate capability.  Conventional carbonate-based electrolytes encounter numerous obstacles for their wide application in SIBs due to the formation of a dissolvable, continuous-thickening solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer and inferior stability with electrodes.  Comparatively, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are emerging in the secondary battery field with fascinating properties to improve the performance of batteries, esp. SIBs.  Their stable solvation structure enables highly reversible solvent-co-intercalation reactions and the formation of a thin and stable SEI.  However, although EBEs can provide more stable cycling and rapid sodiation kinetics in electrodes, benefitting from their favorable electrolyte/electrode interactions such as chem. compatibility and good wettability, their special chem. is still being investigated and puzzling.  In this review, we provide a thorough and comprehensive overview on the developmental history, fundamental characteristics, superiorities and mechanisms of EBEs, together with their advances in other battery systems.  Notably, the relation among electrolyte science, interfacial chem. and electrochem. performance is highlighted, which is of great significance for the in-depth understanding of battery chem.  Finally, future perspectives and potential directions are proposed to navigate the design and optimization of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces for advanced batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCtrhQIYoqYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_a3lD_XDaDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1Gjsb7I&amp;md5=2bd8c004f3d333b92d12cbc8ce920ad6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.136344"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, M.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-stable sodium ion storage of biomass porous carbon derived from sugarcane</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Minjun; Fernando, Joseph F. S.; Li, Zhibin; Alowasheeir, Azhar; Ashok, Aditya; Xin, Ruijing; Martin, Darren; Kumar Nanjundan, Ashok; Golberg, Dmitri V.; Yamauchi, Yusuke; Amiralian, Nasim; Li, Jinliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">445</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of low-cost anode for sodium-ion battery (NIB) has become the most desirable target in todays energy demanding society.  In this work, we present different treatments of sugarcane biomass to alter the lignocellulose compns. to obtain low-cost porous carbon as NIBs anode.  The optimized sugarcane biomass derived carbon presents the initial reversible capacity of 229 mAh g-1 and the reversible capacity of 189 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles.  It is worth noting that the carbon also exhibits an extremely low voltage plateau with 74.2% of discharge capacity originating from the voltages below 0.5 V.  In addn., the sugarcane biomass derived carbon displays an ultra-stable capacity with almost no attenuation even after 2000 cycles.  In consideration of the low voltage plateau, we also calcd. the relative energy d. (ER, combination of the capacity and voltage plateau), and a high ER of 500 Wh kg-1 in the first cycle and 416 Wh kg-1 after 50 cycles are obtained.  In situ TEM anal. was conducted to investigate the structural stability of sugarcane biomass derived carbon.  Small volumetric changes are obsd. at different charge-discharge states, indicating the structural stability of our sugarcane biomass derived carbon during sodiation-desodiation process, which is conducive to the stable cycling of Na-ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpY7dEpnsvbrbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_a3lD_XDaDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1ensbfE&amp;md5=1d87f3bc45f0e800121eaa84ad623e91</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.34133/energymatadv.0012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, S.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NiS2/FeS heterostructured nanoflowers for high-performance sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Dong; Xiao, Shuhao; Li, Xinyan; Jiang, Jinxia; He, Qiyuan; Li, Hanchao; Qin, Jiaqian; Wu, Rui; Niu, Xiaobin; Chen, Jun Song</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy Material Advances</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides demonstrate attractive potential for sodium storage owing to their high theor. specific capacity and high reserve.  However, the low cond. and vol. expansion deteriorate their high-rate performance and cycling stability.  In this work, we construct NiS2/FeS heterostructure by growing Ni-based layered double hydroxide nanosheets on Fe-based Prussian Blue nanocrystals followed by gaseous sulfurization, giving rise to flower-like NiS2/FeS nanoparticles.  The as-prepd. nanocomposite exhibits good rate performance of 156 mAh g-1 at 50 A g-1 and long cycle life of 606 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 1,000 cycles, which are superior to the heterostructure-free counterpart of NiS2 and FeS.  D. functional theory calcn. further verifies that the enhanced electrochem. performance of NiS2/ FeS is due to the existence of interface derived from the heterostructure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSHsLJ0elvWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_a3lD_XDaDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXpvFGhu7g%253D&amp;md5=c657fc80ca70517c95b79c4033b8d77a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.9b01900"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Q.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tuning the Closed Pore Structure of Hard Carbons with the Highest Na Storage Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Meng, Qingshi; Lu, Yaxiang; Ding, Feixiang; Zhang, Qiangqiang; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2608-2612</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-capacity anode materials are one of the bottlenecks to further improve the energy d. of Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Except for introducing more defects to increase the sloping capacity, tuning the closed porous structure to boost the plateau capacity is another direction.  Here by adopting phenol-formaldehyde resin (PF) as the carbon precursor and ethanol (EtOH) as the pore-forming agent, through precise chem. regulation of their relative content during a solvothermal process before further carbonization, carbon anodes with appropriate microstructure are achieved.  It is found that the function of EtOH rests on generating steam vapor to create a pore cavity among cross-linked matrixes.  The obtained optimal anodes exhibit a high Na storage capacity of ca. 410 mAh/g.  When pairing with an O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, the full cell delivers a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 83% and energy d. of ca. 300 Wh/kg.  The proposed chem. regulation approach via a pore-forming strategy is simple and practical to enable high-energy-d. NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrx98YwmwyHobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf4E6os2gTPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFWisrjF&amp;md5=b4f7015f8784563858ca8521e7e095c1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.8b01690"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of Microporous Sulfur-Doped Carbon Microtubes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qiaoqiao; Ge, Xufang; Xu, Jingyi; Du, Yichen; Zhao, Xin; Si, Ling; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing efficient anode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) is important for the storage of renewable energy.  Inspired by the rapid development of biomass-derived hard carbons and heteroatom-doped C materials in various areas, a high-temp. sulfurizing method is exploited for the fabrication of S-doped C microtubes (S-CMTs).  Owing to high S doping (10.2 wt.%) and well-developed microporous structure, the as-prepd. S-CMTs show a large charge capacity of 532 mAh/g at a current rate of 200 mA/g, outstanding rate capability (234 mAh/g at 2 A/g), and exceptional cycling stability (281 mAh/g after 1000 cycles at 1 A/g), values that are superior to those of biomass-derived carbons reported previously.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Capacity Interstitial Mn-Incorporated MnxFe3-xO4/Graphene Nanocomposite for Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ren, Haixia; Bai, Ying; Wang, Xinran; Ni, Qiao; Wang, Zhaohua; Li, Yu; Chen, Guanghai; Wu, Feng; Xu, Huajie; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted wide attention because of their prospects for grid-scale elec. regulation and cost effectiveness of Na.  In this regard, FeOx are considered as one of the most promising anode candidates due to their high theor. capacity and low cost.  Unfortunately, the utilization of FeOx anodes suffers from sluggish reaction kinetics and significant lattice variation, causing insufficient rate performance and fast capacity degrdn. during the sodiation/desodiation process.  Here, Mn ions are incorporated through interstitial sites into a Fe3O4 lattice to form the Mn-incorporated Fe3O4/graphene (M-Fe3O4/G) composites through a facile hydrothermal method.  Confirmed by XRD Rietveld refinement and the first-principles calcn., Mn occupation into the body structure can effectively condense the electron d. around the Fermi level and thus contributes to the increased elec. cond. and improved electrochem. properties.  Accordingly, the M0.1Fe2.9O4/G composite demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 439.8 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g over 200 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 1 A/g, the M-Fe3O4/G composites remain stable for over 1200 cycles, delivering a capacity of 210 mAh/g.  Coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3-type cathode, the Mn-incorporated Fe3O4/G composites demonstrate good suitability in full SIBs (161.2 mAh/g at the c.d. of 1 A/g after 100 cycles).  The regulation of Mn ions in the Fe3O4 lattice provides insights into the optimization of metal oxide anode candidates for their application in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoLIjM225dS7bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf4E6os2gTPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsl2htLnN&amp;md5=f5e5c9968f75a64be4be5ce758cc9f18</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA11273A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A general strategy for embedding ultrasmall CoMx nanocrystals (M = S, O, Se, and Te) in hierarchical porous carbon nanofibers for high-performance potassium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lai, Chenling; Zhang, Zhuangzhuang; Xu, Yifan; Liao, Jiaying; Xu, Zhenhua; Yi, Zuyue; Xu, Jingyi; Bao, Jianchun; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Closely integrated transition-metal-based compds./carbon nanoarchitectures are one of the most promising anode materials for large-scale energy storage applications because of the superior structural stability and the outstanding synergistic effect from the efficient combination of the two components.  Herein, a versatile strategy is demonstrated for fabricating hierarchical porous carbon nanofibers (HCFs) with closely coupled Co-based ultrafine nanoparticles and a carbon matrix.  The spatially restricted reactions of the synthetic method can not only prevent the agglomeration of the nanoparticles, but also provide extremely tight coupling interaction between CoMx (M = S, O, Se, and Te) nanoparticles and conductive carbon nanofibers.  As a proof of concept, the as-fabricated CoS2@HCFs show high reversible capacity, excellent rate property, and ultralong cycling life when evaluated as an anode material for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  Even after 1000 cycles, the charge capacity can be retained at 268 mA h g-1 at an elevated current rate of 500 mA g-1, one of the highest reported performances for Co-based anode materials in PIBs.  This work emphasizes the importance of designing and manufg. highly functionally coupled hybrid materials for improved energy storage implementation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqy1jHZdRWoELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgf4E6os2gTPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXis1Gms7%252FJ&amp;md5=e6be496a6a83768f5592a1f27586df82</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.3866/pku.whxb202205017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod array anodes with high capacity and rate capability for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Liying; Xu, Yang; Wang, Chengliang; Wen, Liaoyong; Fang, Yaoguo; Mi, Yan; Zhou, Min; Zhao, Huaping; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2954-2962</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are a potential substitute to Li-ion batteries for energy storage devices.  However, their poor electrochem. performance, esp. capacity and rate capability, is the major bottleneck to future development.  Here we propose a performance-oriented electrode structure, which is 1D nanostructure arrays with large-scale high ordering, good vertical alignment, and large interval spacing.  Benefiting from these structural merits, a great enhancement in electrochem. performance could be achieved.  Taking Sb as an example, we firstly report large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod arrays with uniform large interval spacing (190 nm).  In return for this electrode design, high ion accessibility, fast electron transport, and strong electrode integrity are presented here.  Used as additive- and binder-free anodes for Na-ion batteries, Sb nanorod arrays showed a high capacity of 620 mA h g-1 at the 100th cycle with a retention of 84% up to 250 cycles at 0.2 A g-1, and a superior rate capability for delivering reversible capacities of 579.7 and 557.7 mA h g-1 at 10 and 20 A g-1, resp.  A full cell coupled by a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathode and a Sb nanorod array anode was also constructed, which showed good cycle performance up to 250 cycles, high rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and large energy d. up to 130 Wh kg-1.  These excellent electrochem. performances shall pave the way for developing more applications of Sb nanorod arrays in energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRS7y0VfakjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbw2Mt4evXUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFGns7nO&amp;md5=50b74924c2a93cc137e8a9993ce641fa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202300002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interfacial-Catalysis-Enabled Layered and Inorganic-Rich SEI on Hard Carbon Anodes in Ester Electrolytes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Mingquan; Wu, Feng; Gong, Yuteng; Li, Yu; Li, Ying; Feng, Xin; Li, Qiaojun; Wu, Chuan; Bai, Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2300002</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a homogenous and inorg.-rich solid electrolyte interface (SEI) can efficiently improve the overall sodium-storage performance of hard carbon (HC) anodes.  However, the thick and heterogenous SEI derived from conventional ester electrolytes fails to meet the above requirements.  Herein, an innovative interfacial catalysis mechanism is proposed to design a favorable SEI in ester electrolytes by reconstructing the surface functionality of HC, of which abundant CO (carbonyl) bonds are accurately and homogenously implanted.  The CO (carbonyl) bonds act as active centers that controllably catalyze the preferential redn. of salts and directionally guide SEI growth to form a homogenous, layered, and inorg.-rich SEI.  Therefore, excessive solvent decompn. is suppressed, and the interfacial Na+ transfer and structural stability of SEI on HC anodes are greatly promoted, contributing to a comprehensive enhancement in sodium-storage performance.  The optimal anodes exhibit an outstanding reversible capacity (379.6 mAh g-1), an ultrahigh initial Coulombic efficiency (93.2%), a largely improved rate capability, and an extremely stable cycling performance with a capacity decay rate of 0.0018% for 10 000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  This work provides novel insights into smart regulation of interface chem. to realize high-performance HC anodes for sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGri_TRbZlnL0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbw2Mt4evXUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhtFantbjP&amp;md5=82764fa5c85e5f6fe482864d43ec6ffa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202106980"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2106980</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202106980</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2106980%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D2%26author%3DX.%2BW.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BY.%2BSun%26author%3DW.%2BX.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BJ.%2BLai%26author%3DX.%2BYu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26title%3DIntergrowth%2Bof%2BGraphite-Like%2BCrystals%2Bin%2BHard%2BCarbon%2Bfor%2BHighly%2BReversible%2BNa-Ion%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202106980&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202106980&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intergrowth of Graphite-Like Crystals in Hard Carbon for Highly Reversible Na-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xianwei; Sun, Jingying; Zhao, Wenxia; Lai, Yongjian; Yu, Xiao; Liu, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2106980</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon usually refers to non-graphitizable carbon, which does not transform into a crystal structure even at high temps.  Although hard carbon is considered as the most promising anode material for Na-ion batteries (NIBs), its practical application is still hindered by its low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE).  Here, the intergrowth of large area graphite-like crystals in hard carbon is reported using cotton as precursor and graphite as crystal template by calcination under their intimate contact condition.  Extensive characterizations provide abundant evidence that graphite-like crystal is a new carbon allotrope belonging to the hexagonal system (a = b = 3.528 S, c = 9.6 S, α = β = 90°, γ = 120°) with d-spacing of 4.8 S for (002) plane.  Its unit cell dimensions and d-spacing of (002) plane are all enlarged by the same factor of 1.428 compared to those of the graphite phase.  When applied in NIBs, the hard carbon with graphite-like crystals shows an extremely high ICE of 95.0% with a large reversible capacity of 343 mAh g-1, which reaches the same level as graphite used in Li-ion batteries.  The graphite-like crystal breaks the traditional concept of hard carbon, while the graphite-template induced epitaxial growth mechanism may provide a new way for obtaining novel cryst. carbon allotropes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrN6OVjZP5yDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbw2Mt4evXUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXit1Sqt7zE&amp;md5=4e3934cac49c88747a387833292dc253</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202109282"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X. J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enabling Fast Na<sup>+</sup> Transfer Kinetics in the Whole-Voltage-Region of Hard-Carbon Anodes for Ultrahigh-Rate Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/adma.202109282</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D34%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2109282%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26issue%3D13%26author%3DX.%2BP.%2BYin%26author%3DZ.%2BX.%2BLu%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BC.%2BFeng%26author%3DS.%2BRoy%26author%3DX.%2BS.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BF.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BJ.%2BZhang%26title%3DEnabling%2BFast%2BNa%252B%2BTransfer%2BKinetics%2Bin%2Bthe%2BWhole-Voltage-Region%2Bof%2BHard-Carbon%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BUltrahigh-Rate%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202109282&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202109282&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enabling Fast Na+ Transfer Kinetics in the Whole-Voltage-Region of Hard-Carbon Anodes for Ultrahigh-Rate Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Xiuping; Lu, Zhixiu; Wang, Jing; Feng, Xiaochen; Roy, Swagata; Liu, Xiangsi; Yang, Yong; Zhao, Yufeng; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2109282</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Efficient electrode materials, that combine high power and high energy, are the crucial requisites of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), which have unwrapped new possibilities in the areas of grid-scale energy storage.  Hard carbons (HCs) are considered as the leading candidate anode materials for SIBs, however, the primary challenge of slow charge-transfer kinetics at the low potential region (&lt;0.1 V) remains unresolved till date, and the underlying structure-performance correlation is under debate.  Herein, ultrafast sodium storage in the whole-voltage-region (0.01-2 V), with the Na+ diffusion coeff. enhanced by 2 orders of magnitude (≈10-7 cm2 s-1) through rationally deploying the phys. parameters of HCs using a ZnO-assisted bulk etching strategy is reported.  It is unveiled that the Na+ adsorption energy (Ea) and diffusion barrier (Eb) are in a pos. and neg. linear relationship with the carbon p-band center, resp., and balance of Ea and Eb is crit. in enhancing the charge-storage kinetics.  The charge-storage mechanism in HCs is evidenced through comprehensive in(ex) situ techniques.  The as prepd. HCs microspheres deliver a record high rate performance of 107 mAh g-1 @ 50 A g-1 and unprecedented electrochem. performance at extremely low temp. (426 mAh g-1 @ -40°C).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZUKSxfBJiLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbw2Mt4evXUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XkvFShsLc%253D&amp;md5=865898bc8fbf211a547b34c3e49e9f46</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2023.170481"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, D.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon anode from carbon dots-regulated polypyrrole for enhanced potassium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Lin; Cheng, Deliang; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo; Yang, Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">958</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aiming at the problems of poor cycle stability of carbon-based materials in potassium ion batteries, functionalized nitrogen and sulfur co-doped carbon dots (CDs) are applied to improve the potassium storage performance of electrode materials.  In this work, the functionalized CDs are used to regulate the structure and morphol. of the polypyrrole in-situ during the polymn. process of pyrrole monomer.  Concretely, the original strip-like fibrous polypyrrole can be induced to become bead-like particle with the disappearance of fiber shape, and with the increase of the amt. of carbon dots, the active particles increased.  Compared with pure polypyrrole derived carbon, the carbon-dot-regulated polypyrrole derived carbon exhibits more excellent cycling performances with a shorter ion transmission and transfer path, more active sites, increased contact area with the electrolyte and improved structural stability.  The specific capacity of the carbon anode carbonized from polypyrrole (C-ppy-NSCDs-100) regulated by 100 mg of carbon dots could reach 360.2 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, showing the application potential of carbon dots in improving electrochem. potassium storage by regulating the morphol. of carbon-based materials.  Predictably, these unparalleled features of CDs can be expected to inspire more exciting results in potassium-ion energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcA9gxooKPiLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbw2Mt4evXUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhtVSls7jI&amp;md5=4f3856ab05c2958350b00bf104883728</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c18464"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, L.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Different Nitrogen Configurations on Sodium Storage Properties of Carbon Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Zheng, Lumin; Liu, Mingquan; Li, Ying; Zhao, Ran; Li, Yu; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen doping carbon materials are considered to be promising candidates for Na+ storage anodes.  However, hitherto, the effects and mechanism of specific single N configuration (among pyrrolic N, quaternary N, and pyridinic N), on the sodium storage behaviors of carbon materials, are still puzzling, owing to the difficulties in accurately synthesizing a certain type of single N configuration dominated carbon materials (NCDCMs).  Here, various NCDCMs have been successfully controlled and synthesized by small mol. polymn. methods, and their synthesis process has been also verified by NMR, MOLDI-TOF, TG-MS, etc.  When serving as sodium ion battery anodes, the NCDCMs dominated by a high concn. of pyrrolic N (&gt;80.3%) exhibits a satisfactory reversible capacity (434.5 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and 146.7 mA h g-1 at 2000 mA g-1, resp.).  It is revealed that pyrrolic N has more suitable adsorption energy and larger interlayer spacing, by d. functional theory calcns. and electron orbital theory, resp., which synergistically makes the material obtain excellent electrochem. performance.  This research exhibits a more efficient way to reveal the differences in the sodium ions storage behavior of different nitrogen configurations doped carbon, and provides new insight for the precise design and synthesis of a certain type of heteroatom doping to achieve satisfactory electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpe4ZR86bfXB7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyOs_w3zD4zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXisVylsbbL&amp;md5=b5eda33ad299d9bff63a240f0d631927</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.104219"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sulphur-doped carbon nanosheets derived from biomass as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Gongyuan; Yu, Dengfeng; Zhang, Hong; Sun, Feifei; Li, Jiwei; Zhu, Lin; Sun, Lei; Yu, Miao; Besenbacher, Flemming; Sun, Ye</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">67</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104219</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted enormous attention as a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries in recent years due to the richness and low cost of sodium (Na) resource.  The SIBs performance is essentially detd. by the electrode materials applied.  Due to the difficulty of intercalating the large Na ions, developing competent anode materials (AMs) has become particularly fascinating and crit. for SIBs.  Herein, three-dimensional (3D) scaffolding framework of carbon nanosheets heavily-doped with sulfur (S-CNS) has been fabricated from plant biomass using a facile thermal method.  The S-CNS affords an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 605 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1, high rate performance 133 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1, and long-term cycling stability at 5 A g-1 (∼94% retention upon 2000 cycles).  These values are among the best results based on AMs of doped carbon derived from biomass ever reported.  Moreover, we demonstrate that such S-doped carbon materials with competent electrochem. properties can be easily produced from diverse plant wastes using this method.  This work thus introduces a universal strategy and a fertile ground to produce high-performance AMs by using the mixt. of biomass and S powder, which may hold considerable potential for scalable prodn. of com. SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGra5olrU5vSSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyOs_w3zD4zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFKrtr3M&amp;md5=d2dfddcc08b583b1c92979075a043098</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202100808"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Increasing Accessible Subsurface to Improving Rate Capability and Cycling Stability of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Bo; Liang, Shuquan; Yu, Dongdong; Cheng, Boshi; Egun, Ishioma L.; Lin, Jiande; Xie, Xuefang; Shao, Hezhu; He, Haiyong; Pan, Anqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2100808</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Numerous studies have reported that the enhancement of rate capability of carbonaceous anode by heteroatom doping is due to the increased diffusion-controlled capacity induced by expanding interlayer spacing.  However, percentage of diffusion-controlled capacity is less than 30% as scan rate is larger than 1 mV s-1, suggesting there is inaccuracy in recognizing principle of improving rate capability of carbonaceous anode.  In this paper, it is found that the heteroatom doping has little impact on interlayer spacing of carbon in bulk phase, meaning that diffusion-controlled capacity is hard to be enhanced by doping.  After synergizing with tensile stress, however, the interlayer spacing in subsurface region is obviously expanded to 0.40 nm, which will increase the thickness of accessible subsurface region at high c.d.  So SRNDC-700 electrodes display a high specific capacity of 160.6 and 69.5 mAh g-1 at 20 and 50 A g-1, resp.  Addnl., the high reversibility of carbon structure insures ultralong cycling stability and hence attenuation of SRNDC-700 is only 0.0025% per cycle even at 10 A g-1 for 6000 cycles.  This report sheds new insight into mechanism of improving electrochem. performance of carbonaceous anode by doping and provides a novel design concept for doping carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpUbWnwUlqVGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyOs_w3zD4zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslyksLnJ&amp;md5=bdd43c9aaad0af76a8349314e1e07874</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/inf2.12231"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Catalytic Defect-Repairing Using Manganese Ions for Hard Carbon Anode with High-Capacity and High-Initial-Coulombic-Efficiency in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Jiahua; He, Xiang-Xi; Lai, Wei-Hong; Yang, Zhuo; Liu, Xiao-Hao; Li, Lin; Qiao, Yun; Xiao, Yao; Li, Li; Wu, Xingqiao; Chou, Shu-Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) anodes have shown extraordinary promise for sodium-ion batteries, but are limited to their poor initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) and low practical specific capacity due to the large amt. of defects.  These defects with oxygen contg. groups cause irreversible sites for Na+ ions.  Highly graphited carbon decreases defects, while potentially blocking diffusion paths of Na+ ions.  Therefore, mol.-level control of graphitization of hard carbon with open accessible channels for Na+ ions is key to achieve high-performance hard carbon.  Moreover, it is challenging to design a conventional method to obtain HCs with both high ICE and capacity.  Herein, a universal strategy is developed as manganese ions-assisted catalytic carbonization to precisely tune graphitization degree, eliminate defects, and maintain effective Na+ ions paths.  The as-prepd. hard carbon has a high ICE of 92.05% and excellent cycling performance.  Simultaneously, a sodium storage mechanism of "adsorption-intercalation-pore filling-sodium cluster formation" is proposed, and a clear description given of the boundaries of the pore structure and the specific dynamic process of pore filling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpl6mTs0uPrkrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyOs_w3zD4zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXms1OqsL0%253D&amp;md5=b065864d193df474808b4224e1432ca1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.34133/2022/9896218"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doped carbon is an attractive material for anodes in lithium-/sodium-ion batteries as a replacement for traditional graphite anodes.  However, the complex fabrication process and high cost limit practical applications of these carbon materials.  Here, a low-cost, natural potassium-doped carbon material is reported which is directly carbonized from the coconut endocarp, a kind of high potassium-contg. biomass material.  The obtained carbon structure features an expanded d(002)-spacing (0.4 nm) originating from the superhigh potassium content (6654 mg kg-1).  Because of the improvement on charge transfer kinetics and elec. properties, the potassium-doped carbon anode exhibits promising electrochem. performance in sodium-ion batteries, including high initial reversible capacity (314 mAh g-1) and good cycle stability (289 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles).                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Zinc Single-Atom-Regulated Hard Carbons for High-Rate and Low-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Zhixiu; Wang, Jing; Feng, Wuliang; Yin, Xiuping; Feng, Xiaochen; Zhao, Shengyu; Li, Caixia; Wang, Ruixiao; Huang, Qiu-An; Zhao, Yufeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons, as one of the most commercializable anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), have to deal with the trade-off between the rate capability and specific capacity or initial Columbic efficiency (ICE), and the fast performance decline at low temp. (LT) remains poorly understood.  Here, a comprehensive regulation on the interfacial/bulk electrochem. of hard carbons through at. Zn doping is reported, which demonstrates a record-high reversible capacity (546 mAh g-1), decent ICE (84%), remarkable rate capability (140 mAh g-1 @ 50 A g-1), and excellent LT capacity (443 mAh g-1 @ -40 °C), outperforming the state-of-the-art literature.  This work reveals that the Zn doping can generally induce a local elec. field to enable fast bulk Na+ transportation, and meanwhile catalyze the decompn. of NaPF6 to form a robust inorg.-rich solid-electrolyte interphase, which elaborates the underlying origin of the boosted electrochem. performance.  Importantly, distinguished from room temp., the intrinsic Na+ migration/desolvation ability of the electrolyte is disclosed to be the crucial rate-detg. factors for the SIB performance at LT.  This work provides a fundamental understanding on the charge-storage kinetics at varied temps.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqw4sUUi9VQbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHSq2guqtVtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXpvV2qtbY%253D&amp;md5=2ac47b97eaf62a0a764121cf7bd51b53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1007/s40843-022-2176-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.
