                10.1007/s40843-022-2176-6</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D66%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D541-555%26journal%3DSci.%2BChina%2BMater.%26issue%3D2%26author%3DM.%2BQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DY.%2BH.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BM.%2BZheng%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BT.%2BGong%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26title%3DMolecular%2BEngineering%2Btoward%2BSustainable%2BDevelopment%2Bof%2BMultiple-Doped%2BHierarchical%2BPorous%2BCarbons%2Bfor%2BSuperior%2BZinc%2BIon%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs40843-022-2176-6&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs40843-022-2176-6&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molecular engineering toward sustainable development of multiple-doped hierarchical porous carbons for superior zinc ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Mingquan; Wu, Feng; Feng, Xin; Wang, Yahui; Zheng, Lumin; Li, Xin; Li, Ying; Gong, Yuteng; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science China Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">66</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">541-555</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCMCDB</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-8226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science China Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors (ZHSCs) hold great potential as next-generation energy storage devices due to their low cost, excellent rate capability, long cycling life, and high safety.  Heteroatom-doped hierarchical porous carbons (HD-HPCs) with integrated high sp. surface area, multiscale pores, and abundant defects have been regarded as promising cathode materials for ZHSCs.  However, the in situ architecture of HD-HPCs with these multiple advantages via a sustainable and controllable method remains an arduous challenge.  Herein, a novel mol. engineering strategy was proposed for the in situ construction of N/P/O-doped HD-HPCs via the direct carbonization of multiple-heteroatom-rich hypermols.  Such a strategy has multiple advantages, including the exclusion of pore-making techniques, activation agents, templates, and complicated and hazard washing processes, demonstrating its green and sustainable properties.  The highly active multiple-heteroatom-rich hypermol. precursors contributed to the formation of abundant micro/mesopores due to the self-abscission of heteroatoms and heteroatom-contiguous carbon atoms at high carbonization temps.  Consequently, these active structural/compositional features endowed the optimal cathodes with outstanding storage capacities of 139.2 and 88.9 mA h g-1 at 0.5 and 20 A g-1 for aq. ZHSCs, resp.  They also delivered a superior storage performance in quasi-solid ZHSCs (QS-ZHSCs) with a high specific capacity of 111.5 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1.  Superior energy/power densities and long cycling stability were also achieved for aq. and QS-ZHSCs.  The theor. calcn. confirmed the synergetic effects of multiple-atom doping on enhancing the electronic cond. and reducing the energy barrier between Zn ions and carbon, which promote the Zn-ion adsorption capability.  These findings shed fresh light on the straightforward manuf. of superior HD-HPCs for electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmNnWMP3uX8bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHSq2guqtVtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVOmsrnK&amp;md5=d92b2d12ab531c094f14541fe9e84980</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202200886"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Overall understanding of sodium storage behaviors in hard carbon by adsorption-intercalation/filling hybrid mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaoyang; Tian, Jiyu; Li, Peng; Fang, Youlong; Fang, Yongjin; Liang, Xinmiao; Feng, Jiwen; Dong, Jiao; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2200886</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon has the potential to serve as a high-capacity anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), however, its Na+ storage mechanism, particularly on the low potential plateau, remains controversial.  To overcome this issue, two types of hard carbons with different microstructures are employed and the relationship between the microstructures and Na+ storage behaviors is evaluated.  By the combination of operando X-ray diffraction, ex situ Raman spectroscopy, NMR, and theor. calcn., it is found that the sodium storage capacities of the hard carbons in the low potential plateau region contain the concurrent contributions from both interlayer intercalation and micropores filling, and the ratio of the two contributors greatly depends on the microstructure of hard carbon materials.  Moreover, an electrochem. pointer (potential inflection point at the end of the discharge curve) is found to distinguish the dominance of interlayer intercalation and the micropores filling processes of sodium ions in the low potential plateau region.  Based on this new finding, a microstructure-dependent mechanism ("adsorption-intercalation/filling" hybrid mechanism) is proposed to achieve an overall understanding of the sodium storage behaviors in different hard carbon materials, which may provide deep insight into the rational design of hard carbon structures as high-performance anode materials for advanced SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrd5o_TaI-O_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHSq2guqtVtQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1agu7nK&amp;md5=9f95b49d8ff9183780d72d7341aea49b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202308392"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Revealing the closed pore formation of waste wood-derived hard carbon for advanced sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Zheng; Zhang, Rui; Wang, Haiyan; Zhou, Siyu; Pan, Zhiyi; Huang, Yuancheng; Sun, Dan; Tang, Yougen; Ji, Xiaobo; Amine, Khalil; Shao, Minhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6024</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although the closed pore structure plays a key role in contributing low-voltage plateau capacity of hard carbon anode for sodium-ion batteries, the formation mechanism of closed pores is still under debate.  Here, we employ waste wood-derived hard carbon as a template to systematically establish the formation mechanisms of closed pores and their effect on sodium storage performance.  We find that the high crystallinity cellulose in nature wood decomps. to long-range carbon layers as the wall of closed pore, and the amorphous component can hinder the graphitization of carbon layer and induce the crispation of long-range carbon layers.  The optimized sample demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 430 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1 (plateau capacity of 293 mAh g-1 for the second cycle), as well as good rate and stable cycling performances (85.4% after 400 cycles at 500 mA g-1).                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">From micropores to ultra-micropores inside hard carbon: toward enhanced capacity in room-/ low-temperature sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Jinlin; Wang, Xiaowei; Dai, Wenrui; Lian, Xu; Cui, Xinhang; Zhang, Weichao; Zhang, Kexin; Lin, Ming; Zou, Ruqiang; Loh, Kian Ping; Yang, QuanHong; Chen, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano-Micro Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">98</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NLAEBV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2150-5551</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nano-Micro Letters</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pore structure of hard carbon has a fundamental influence on the electrochem. properties in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Ultra-micropores (&lt; 0.5 nm) of hard carbon can function as ionic sieves to reduce the diffusion of slovated Na+ but allow the entrance of naked Na+ into the pores, which can reduce the interficial contact between the electrolyte and the inner pores without sacrificing the fast diffusion kinetics.  Herein, a molten diffusion-carbonization method is proposed to transform the micropores (&gt; 1 nm) inside carbon into ultra-micropores (&lt; 0.5 nm).  Consequently, the designed carbon anode displays an enhanced capacity of 346 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 with a high ICE value of ∼ 80.6% and most of the capacity (∼ 90%) is below 1 V.  Moreover, the high-loading electrode (∼ 19 mg cm-2) exhibits a good temp. endurance with a high areal capacity of 6.14 mAh cm-2 at 25°C and 5.32 mAh cm-2 at - 20°C.  Based on the in situ X-ray diffraction and ex situ solid-state NMR results, the designed ultra-micropores provide the extra Na+ storage sites, which mainly contributes to the enhanced capacity.  This proposed strategy shows a good potential for the development of high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoC346bmDVQirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6JlJILBRmiw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsFGktbnF&amp;md5=9bb97865bf7693f158a29ff3825c07d8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.202100580"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, Q.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons are promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the low practical capacity from limited sodiation sites impedes their applications.  Herein, ultrahigh concn. of pyridine N (≈7.9%) is introduced inside hard carbon, considering that pyridine N may provide extra sodium storage sites with stable CN• and CC• radicals during cycling.  To expose more radical sites for sodium storage, a 3D structure with a multistage pore structure is constructed through NH3 release during the pyrolyzation process.  As expected, the hard carbon with extra sodiation sites exhibits an impressively high capacity of 434 mA h g-1 at 20 mA g-1, superior rate performance of 238 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 5 A g-1 and a high-capacity retention of 98.7% after 5000 cycles.  The radicals induced Na-adsorption mechanism was further explored through ex situ ESR technol., in situ Raman technol. and d. functional theory calcns.  The results reveal that the extra sodiation sites come from the electrostatic interaction at low potentials.  This work constructs a sodium ions storage model of extra radicals and provides an extended strategy to improve the electrochem. performance of SIBs anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmqI1aXQt7hLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6JlJILBRmiw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhvVKmu7w%253D&amp;md5=22397f4aa97787e5332338e00fa064fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b05085"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Estevez, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prabhakaran, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Garcia, A.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically Porous Graphitic Carbon with Simultaneously High Surface Area and Colossal Pore Volume Engineered via Ice Templating</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Estevez, Luis; Prabhakaran, Venkateshkumar; Garcia, Adam L.; Shin, Yongsoon; Tao, Jinhui; Schwarz, Ashleigh M.; Darsell, Jens; Bhattacharya, Priyanka; Shutthanandan, Vaithiyalingam; Zhang, Ji-Guang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing hierarchical porous carbon (HPC) materials with competing textural characteristics such as surface area and pore vol. in one material is difficult to accomplish, particularly for an atomically ordered graphitic carbon.  Herein we describe a synthesis strategy to engineer tunable HPC materials across micro-, meso-, and macroporous length scales, allowing the fabrication of a graphitic HPC material (HPC-G) with both very high surface area (&gt;2500 m2/g) and pore vol. (&gt;11 cm3/g), the combination of which has not been attained previously.  The mesopore vol. alone for these materials is up to 7.53 cm3/g, the highest ever reported, higher than even any porous carbon's total pore vol., which for our HPC-G material was &gt;11 cm3/g.  This HPC-G material was explored for use both as a supercapacitor electrode and for oil adsorption, two applications that require either high surface area or large pore vol., textural properties that are typically exclusive to one another.  We accomplished these high textural characteristics by employing ice templating not only as a route for macroporous formation but as a synergistic vehicle that enabled the significant loading of the mesoporous hard template.  This design scheme for HPC-G materials can be utilized in broad applications, including electrochem. systems such as batteries and supercapacitors, sorbents, and catalyst supports, particularly supports where a high degree of thermal stability is required.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcm2Yys-5vcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6JlJILBRmiw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yhtr%252FM&amp;md5=8c7a956dbe583d6309366fe62f799c15</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202211690"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Diatomite-Templated Synthesis of Single-Atom Cobalt-Doped MoS2/Carbon Composites to Boost Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Xia; Feng, Wang; Li, Xiaohui; Yang, Junbo; Du, Ruofan; Wang, Peng; Li, Hui; Song, Luying; Wang, Yuzu; Cheng, Mo; He, Jun; Shi, Jianping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">2D transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs) and single-atom catalysts (SACs) are promising electrodes for energy conversion/storage because of the layered structure and max. atom utilization efficiency.  However, the integration of such two type materials and the relevant sodium storage applications remain daunting challenges.  Here, an ingenious diatomite-templated synthetic strategy is designed to fabricate single-atom cobalt-doped MoS2/carbon (SA Co-MoS2/C) composites toward the high-performance sodium storage.  Benefiting from the unique hierarchical structure, high electron/sodium-ion cond., and abundant active sites, the obtained SA Co-MoS2/C reveals remarkable specific capacity (≈604.0 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), high rate performance, and outstanding long cyclic stability.  Particularly, the sodium-ion full cell composed of SA Co-MoS2/C anode and Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode demonstrates unexpected stability with the cycle no. exceeded 1200.  The internal sodium storage mechanism is clarified with the aid of d. functional theory calcns. and in situ exptl. characterizations.  This work not only represents a substantial leap in terms of synthesizing SACs on 2D TMDCs but also provides a crucial step toward the practical sodium-ion battery applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrpxMlg1I-J7bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6JlJILBRmiw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhsFOjsb3N&amp;md5=03ef92577d18c0c9f795a2e7f09a944d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.susmat.2020.e00227"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Beda, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Le Meins, J.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Impact of biomass inorganic impurities on hard carbon properties and performance in Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Beda, Adrian; Le Meins, Jean-Marc; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Simon, Patrice; Matei Ghimbeu, Camelia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Materials and Technologies</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Biomass waste recently emerged as efficient precursors for hard carbon anode prepn. for Na-ion batteries.  Despite their very complex microstructure (org./inorg.) there is a lack of knowledge about their impact on carbon formation.  In this paper, the influence of inorg. impurities of three raw local biomass wastes (asparagus, grape and potato) on the hard carbon properties and on their electrochem. performance is investigated, by performing a washing step either before or after the thermal treatment (TT) at 1300°C.  When washing was done after the TT (with HCl), most of cryst. inorg. impurities (K, Ca, Si, Mg - based compds.) could be significantly removed.  This triggered the increase of ultramicroporosity along with mesoporosity formation and graphite interlayer space (d002) contraction.  Such observations are less pronounced on grape derived carbon due to the inorg.'s catalytic induced local graphitization during pyrolysis.  The oxygen content in the pristine carbons was high, owing to the presence of inorg. metal oxides and carbonates, and could be diminished after washing along with the amt. of defects.  Thus, the carbon content and the electronic cond. of the materials were enhanced.  The electrochem. performance improvement after washing was limited since the pos. effect brought by impurities removal was neg. compensated by the changes occurring in the materials, particularly the increase in the sp. surface area.  Diffrently, the washing done before the TT (with water) induced only fewer changes on the materials porosity and structure and slightly improved capacity (from 215 to 230 mAh g-1).  Furthermore, higher pyrolysis temp. (1400°C) on washed HCs afforded a better reversible capacity up to 280 mAh g-1.  This comprehensive study opens the door for green and mild synthesis approach to be further explored for sustainable fabrication of hard carbon for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp43JlypGhvFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6JlJILBRmiw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFShsrjI&amp;md5=f558e31213b80516efd1aa97d4269545</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201801148"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, X.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Impact of the acid treatment on lignocellulosic biomass hard carbon for sodium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dou, Xinwei; Hasa, Ivana; Saurel, Damien; Jauregui, Maria; Buchholz, Daniel; Rojo, Teofilo; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hyperaccumulation Route to Ca-Rich Hard Carbon Materials with Cation Self-Incorporation and Interlayer Spacing Optimization for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Kaihua; Zhao, Huichun; Wang, Xinran; Zhang, Minghao; Dong, Ruiqi; Li, Ying; Bai, Ying; Xu, Huajie; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10544-10553</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The hard carbon (HC) was emerging as one of the most promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Incorporation of cations into HC lattice proved to be effective to regulate their d-interlayer spacing with the modified SIBs performance.  However, the complexity and high-cost of current synthetic processes limited its large-scale application in SIBs.  Through the natural hyperaccumulation process, a cost-effective and scale up-driven procedure to produce Ca-ion self-incorporated HC materials was proposed by applying tamarind fruits as precursor with the enrichment of Ca-ions.  In virtue of one-step pyrolysis, the self-incorporated and well-distributed Ca-ions in tamarind fruits had successfully served as the buffer layer to expand the d-interlayer spacing of HC materials.  Furthermore, the natural porosity hierarchy could be largely preserved by the optimization of calcination temp.  As a result, the Ca-rich HC material had exhibited the optimized cycling performance (326.7 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and capacity retention rate of 89.40% after 250 cycles) with a high initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 70.39%.  This work provided insight on applying the hyperaccumulation effect of biomass precursors to produce doped HC materials with ions self-incorporation and the optimized d-interlayer spacing, navigating its large-scale application for the high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4OqZvNDYxR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9DCkq6VgQVw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisFKrsLg%253D&amp;md5=bcd6ff3deabf3d7b776728e1457119f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA04877C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A waste biomass derived hard carbon as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Pin; Li, Yunming; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13046-13052</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of renewable energies has become increasingly urgent for the sustainable development of our society.  Energy storage systems are essential in order to efficiently use these energies.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) show bright prospect in the application for energy storage markets due to the potential low cost originating from unlimited sources and wide distribution of Na.  However, the anode remains a great challenge in the industrialization of SIBs.  Hard carbon holds the most promising future among all reported anodes; however, there are still two main shortcomings such as high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency, which limit its application.  Here, we report a hard carbon material derived from an abundant and abandoned biomass of corn cobs (HCC) using a simple carbonization method.  The HCC shows excellent sodium storage performance with a reversible capacity of ca. 300 mA h g-1, a high initial coulombic efficiency of 86% and good cycling stability.  A prototype sodium-ion battery was prepd. to prove the application prospect using HCC1300 as the anode and Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 as the cathode, exhibiting a high energy d. of 207 W h kg-1 and a long cycle life.  These excellent properties demonstrate that HCC is a potential candidate as an anode material for sodium-ion battery application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrzP3444VBrIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9DCkq6VgQVw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1eju7nN&amp;md5=f6776d35bde5f3fb873f88fe495141b6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.104038"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, W.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon quantum dot micelles tailored hollow carbon anode for fast potassium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Wanwan; Zhang, Yu; Yang, Li; Tian, Ye; Ge, Peng; Hu, Jiugang; Wei, Weifeng; Zou, Guoqiang; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials are promising anode materials for alkali-metal ion batteries due to the abundant resource and high safety, while it is challenged by its low specific capacity and depressed rate capability in potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  To further explore the potassium storage properties of carbon materials and exploit high-performance carbon anode for PIBs, in this work, hollow nanostructured N-doped carbon (p-HNCs) is elaborately designed through the tailoring of carbon quantum dots (CQDs) for the first time.  The detailed formation mechanism of hollow nanostructure is investigated and it is demonstrated that CQD micelles formed through hydrophobicity and lipophilicity are served not only as templates for the construction of hollow structure but also pore-forming agent for the generation of rich micro-tunnels, due to the decompn. and contraction of CQDs with releasing gases during the pyrolysis process.  When applied for potassium storage, p-HNCs anode delivers high reversible specific capacities of 254 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 100 cycles and 160 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 800 cycles.  Notably, a desirable rate capability of 145 mAh g-1 is obsd. at 4.0 A g-1, derived from surface-driven behaviors.  Moreover, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique measurement quantifies the improved diffusion coeff. of p-HNCs, indicating its superior kinetic property.  This work shows us the special application of CQDs in structure construction and a valuable strategy to design high-performance carbon anode for potassium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxwAeL5ENwDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9DCkq6VgQVw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural Analysis of Sucrose-Derived Hard Carbon and Correlation with the Electrochemical Properties for Lithium, Sodium, and Potassium Insertion</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kubota, Kei; Shimadzu, Saori; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Tominaka, Satoshi; Shiraishi, Soshi; Abreu-Sepulveda, Maria; Manivannan, Ayyakkannu; Gotoh, Kazuma; Fukunishi, Mika; Dahbi, Mouad; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon possesses the ability to store Li, Na, and K ions between stacked sp2 carbon layers and voids (micropores).  We have explored hard carbon as a candidate for neg. electrode materials for Li-ion, Na-ion, and K-ion batteries.  Hard carbon samples have been prepd. by carbonizing sucrose at different heat treatment temps. (HTTs) in the range of 700-2000°C to make them structurally suitable for reversible Li, Na, and K insertion.  Structures and particle morphol. of the hard carbon samples synthesized at different HTTs were systematically characterized using X-ray diffraction, small-angle X-ray scattering, pair distribution function anal., electron microscopy, Raman spectroscopy, and ESR spectroscopy.  All these characterizations of hard carbon samples have revealed advanced ordering of carbons and redn. of carbon defects with increasing HTT.  Thus, the av. stacked carbon interlayer distance decreases, the no. of the stacking layers increases, the layered domains grow in the in-plane direction, and interstitial voids enlarge.  Electrochem. properties of the hard carbons were examd. in nonaq. Li, Na, and K cells.  Potential profiles and reversible capacities upon galvanostatic charge/discharge processes in nonaq. cells are significantly different depending on HTTs and different alkali metal ions.  On the basis of these findings, strategies to design high-capacity hard carbon neg. electrodes for high-energy-d. Li-ion, Na-ion, and K-ion batteries are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr6G6NR3Sjg1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9DCkq6VgQVw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXktlOnurY%253D&amp;md5=39bd5eef10835b2e37215cb7a7f56521</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b01419"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon material is one of the candidates with great promise as anode-active material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Here, new types of biomass-derived hard carbons were obtained via one-step carbonization of lotus seedpods at 1000-1400°, resp.  The control of carbonization temp. proved to be significant in controlling the lattice characterization of lotus seedpod-derived hard carbon.  Higher temp. generally promoted the lattice graphitization and thus generated a more narrowed d-interlayer space with limited pore vol.  The hard carbon pyrolyzed at 1200° achieved an optimized reversible capacity of 328.8 mAh g-1 and exhibited a remarkable capacity retention of 90% after 200 cycles.  In addn., such a biomass-derived hard carbon presented improved cyclic stability and rate performance, revealing capacity of 330.6, 288.9, 216.9, 116.5, and 78.3 mAh g-1 at 50, 100, 200, 500, and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Intrinsically, high pyrolysis temp. (1400°) gave rise to more narrowed carbon lattice and reduced pore vol. and, thus, failed to accommodate sodium ions either from the intercalation into lattice or the ion adsorption onto the pore surface.  Such combined advantages of lotus seedpod-derived hard carbon, including the abundance, sufficiently adequate reversible capacity, and prominent cycling and rate property allowed for its large-scale application as promising anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEusCsCPVmQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioVPq_i08tAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXltFCisb8%253D&amp;md5=c24e6a8c5e5878a4b5c35f70ef737928</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/nl300901a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Eckmann, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Felten, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mishchenko, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Britnell, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krupke, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Novoselov, K.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Nature of Defects in Graphene by Raman Spectroscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Eckmann, Axel; Felten, Alexandre; Mishchenko, Artem; Britnell, Liam; Krupke, Ralph; Novoselov, Kostya S.; Casiraghi, Cinzia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Raman spectroscopy is able to probe disorder in graphene through defect-activated peaks.  It is of great interest to link these features to the nature of disorder.  Here the authors present a detailed anal. of the Raman spectra of graphene contg. different type of defects.  The intensity ratio of the D and D' peak is max. (∼13) for sp3-defects, it decreases for vacancy-like defects (∼7), and it reaches a min. for boundaries in graphite (∼3.5).  This makes Raman Spectroscopy a powerful tool to fully characterize graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpby02MgX7xJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioVPq_i08tAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XpvVKlurs%253D&amp;md5=f89193dfcc10578dda22d4474210828a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01394A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kiso, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Horiba, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chafik, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hida, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuyama, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of Hard Carbon from Argan Shells for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of hard carbon from argan shells for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dahbi, Mouad; Kiso, Manami; Kubota, Kei; Horiba, Tatsuo; Chafik, Tarik; Hida, Kazuo; Matsuyama, Takashi; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is an attractive material for neg. electrodes in sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, we report a new hard carbon synthesized via carbonization of argan shell biomass, which delivers an enhanced capacity higher than 330 mA h g-1 based upon reversible sodium insertion.  We prepd. hard carbon under different high-temp. treatment and biomass pretreatment conditions.  The graphitization degree of the hard carbon increased as the carbonization temp. increased; simultaneously, the reversible capacity for sodium storage was significantly influenced by the carbonization temp.  Structural characterization revealed differences in the structures of the hard carbons synthesized at different carbonization temps., which elucidates the correlation between the increased capacity and the micropore size available for sodium storage. The electrodes delivered reversible capacities as high as 300 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 25 mA g-1 with superior reversibility and capacity retention of 94.1% after 70 cycles.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Active sites enriched hard carbon porous nanobelts for stable and high-capacity potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; He, Qiu; Xiong, Fangyu; Zhou, Jinping; Zhao, Yan; Mai, Liqiang; Zhang, Lina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon finds crit. applications in potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) anodes because of its attractive advantages including low cost and high cond.  However, the sluggish reaction kinetics and structural instability caused by large K+ intercalation/deintercalation limit their storage capability and cycling life.  Herein, active sites enriched hard carbon porous nanobelts (NOCNBs) for enhanced K+ storage are constructed from mineralized shrimp shells via a self-template assisted pyrolysis strategy.  The NOCNBs possess multiscale structure with hierarchical micro/meso/macro-pores, high-level pyrrolic/pyridinic-N and O dual-doping, and large interlayer spacing.  Hence, the NOCNBs deliver a high capacity of 468 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and long cycling life (277 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 over 1600 cycles), representing one of the best storage capability and cycling stability among the reported carbonaceous electrodes.  D. functional theory calcns. and kinetic anal. demonstrate that the abundant active sites within NOCNBs can strengthen K adsorption and diffusion, facilitating capacitive-adsorbed storage.  Furthermore, they exhibit a superior capacity of 89 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 for potassium dual-ion batteries (PDIBs).  This work opens up a new avenue for constructing porous hard carbon to achieve excellent K+ storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtyxkCauK8u7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioVPq_i08tAA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVCls7%252FL&amp;md5=47ffd3bb008d85ce0880c21f2a2adced</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.12.103"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although hard carbons have been turned out to be suitable for sodium storage, their high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) need to be addressed for the com. application.  Here, we report an effective route including a pyrolysis process and a reductive strategy to synthesize high-performance hard carbons from waste apricot shell.  The obtained hard carbons inherit the unique architecture of the apricot shell, delivering a large interlayer spacing and a well-connected structure, which are beneficial for the Na+ intercalation and transport.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their high cond. and low cost, carbon materials have attracted great attention in the field of energy storage, esp. as anode material for sodium ion batteries.  Current research focuses on introducing external defects through heteroatom engineering to improve the sodium storage performance of carbon materials.  However, there is still a lack of systematic investigation of the effects of intrinsic defects prevalent in carbon materials on sodium storage performance.  Herein, template-assisted method was used to design carbon materials with different degrees of intrinsic defects and explore their sodium storage properties.  The exptl. results show that the intrinsic defects in the carbon materials facilitates the adsorption behavior of Na+ during the surface induction capacitance process.  Among them, the best carbon anode material exhibits high reversible capacity (221 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1) and excellent rate performance.  In addn., the d. functional theory calcns. also show that the existence of intrinsic defects can optimize the distribution of electron d., thereby increasing the Na-adsorption capacity.  This work makes an important contribution to understanding the role of intrinsic defects in the sodium storage performance of carbon materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomPK-aC-rtdbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-rVogBG85Qw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFSqt7c%253D&amp;md5=fe38cfec869f4d248ae195d817357258</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.susmat.2022.e00446"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon derived from hazelnut shell with facile HCl treatment as high-initial-coulombic-efficiency anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jiacheng; Zhao, Jiahua; He, Xiangxi; Qiao, Yun; Li, Li; Chou, Shu-Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Materials and Technologies</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is an extremely promising anode material for Na-ion batteries owing to its low cost and low operating potential plateau.  However, the practical use of hard carbon materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is greatly constrained by their low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE).  Biomass as carbon sources are a good choice due to the abundance of resources and natural microstructure.  Regrettably, biomass contains many impurities that lower its electrochem. performance.  Here, by facile synthesis methods, we prep. a hard carbon with a high reversible capacity of 342 mA h g-1 and a high ICE of 91%.  The hard carbon is obtained by carbonizing a low-cost biomass hazelnut shell under hydrochloric acid treatment.  Hydrochloric acid treatment removes impurities and change microstructure such as interlayer spacing and active sites.  The results reveal that the active site and interlayer spacing of the hard carbon material was raised with hydrochloric acid treatment.  Therefore, the reversible capacity of hard carbon was greatly improved by the hydrochloric acid treatment.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB1CyaTzGexrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-rVogBG85Qw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xit1SmtrjM&amp;md5=0645dbdfb269d606831757d1dbeca226</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201900005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, Y.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Slope-Dominated Carbon Anode with High Specific Capacity and Superior Rate Capability for High Safety Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qi, Yuruo; Lu, Yaxiang; Ding, Feixiang; Zhang, Qiangqiang; Li, Hong; Huang, Xuejie; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The comprehensive performance of carbon anodes for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is largely restricted by their inferior rate capability and safety issues.  Herein, a slope-dominated carbon anode is achieved at a low temp. of 800°C, which delivers a high reversible capacity of 263 mA h g-1 at 0.15C with an impressive initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 80%.  When paired with the NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, the reversible capacity at 6C is still 75% of that at 0.15C, and 73% of the capacity is retained after 1000 cycles at 3C.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomass-Derived Hard Carbon with Interlayer Spacing Optimization toward Ultrastable Na-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Zhidong; Lei, Da; Jiang, Mingwei; Gao, Yuyang; Zhang, Xiang; Zhang, Yu; Wang, Jian-Gan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons as a kind of nongraphitized amorphous carbon have been recognized as potential anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its large interlayer spacing.  However, the issues in terms of onerous synthetic procedure and elusive working mechanism remains crit. bottlenecks for practical implement.  Herein, we report a facile prodn. of tubular hard carbon through direct carbonization of platanus flosses (FHC) for the first time.  Through optimizing the pyrolysis temps., the FHC obtained at 1300°C possesses a key balance between the interlayer spacing and surface area, which can maintain the substantial active sites as well as reduce the irreversible sodium storage.  Accordingly, it can deliver a reversible capacity of 324.6 mA h g-1 with a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 80%, superb rate property of 107.2 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1, and long operating stability over 1000 cycles.  Furthermore, the in situ Raman spectroscopic studies certify that sodium ions are stored in FHC following the "adsorption-insertion" mechanism.  Our study could provide a promising route for large-scale development of the biomass-derived carbonaceous anodes for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrohOXvskuxVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-rVogBG85Qw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XjtFyhtrfI&amp;md5=f69341fd709598815892f5cbe803f217</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c06168"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tailoring a Phenolic Resin Precursor by Facile Pre-oxidation Tactics to Realize a High-Initial-Coulombic-Efficiency Hard Carbon Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Guifang; Zhang, Lijun; Ren, Qingjuan; Yan, Lei; Zhang, Fuming; Lv, Wenjie; Shi, Zhiqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">31650-31659</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As the leading anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), hard carbon (HC) still faces the puzzle of low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) in achieving commercialization.  From the perspective of precursors, the low ICE has been attributed to the large sp. surface area and porosity produced by the rapid decompn. of polymers during the carbonization.  Therefore, increasing the crosslinking degree of precursors will be an effective shortcut to improve the ICE.  Herein, a facile pre-oxidn. tactic was successfully employed to tailor the crosslinking degree of phenolic resin precursors to precisely control the sp. surface area of the obtained HC.  As the pre-oxidn. time is increased, the optimal HC with the lowest sp. surface area shows an ICE elevated by 22.2% (from 62.5 to 84.7%) compared to the original pre-oxidn. HC and delivers a high reversible capacity of 334.3 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1.  Besides, the pre-oxidn. also introduces abundant carbonyl groups, which increase the disorder degree of HC and supply abundant adsorption sites of Na+, thus enhancing the rate performance.  When matched with a layered O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, the full cell achieves an energy d. of ca. 256.2 Wh kg-1 with superior rate performance.  This work sheds light on the pos. effect of pre-oxidn. in elevating the ICE of HC and provides effective guidance to achieve a high ICE for other HC materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEtifM7H9TxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-rVogBG85Qw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVWrt7bI&amp;md5=c6c2f8486c9b497a858ce1c6b89cd82c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2021.11.064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lyu, L.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into self-induced electrochemical activation of carbon cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lyu, Linlong; Hu, Jing; Cheng, Kui; Lin, Dongmei; Li, Kaikai; Lu, Zhouguang; Yao, Haimin; Zhou, Limin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">188</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Continuous capacity increase in electrochem. cycling, termed as electrochem. activation, is a frequently obsd. but rarely systematically studied phenomenon.  Such phenomenon is noted in a preliminary study of carbon cathode for dual ion battery, showing gradual discharge capacity growth from 186 mAh g-1 (the 1st) to 320 mAh g-1 (the 300th).  Systematical characterizations are carried out to investigate this phenomenon occurred on the carbon cathode, hydrothermally reduced graphene oxide (HrGO).  The electrochem. activation comes from surface area increment, originated from multilayer reduced graphene oxide rolls formation and accumulation and structural order increase in cycling.  The formation of rolls is plausibly a result of strain release of reduced graphene layers after electrochem. interaction with PF-6.  Addnl., charge storage mechanism of HrGO is revealed.  At active surface sites of HrGO, PF-6 is consistently stored in a pseudocapacitive manner.  In contrast, at well-crystd. domains, pseudocapacitive PF-6 uptake occurs at low voltage region while PF-6 intercalation dominates at higher potentials.  Supportive lithium storage also contributes to total capacity.  Comprehensively, this work offers valuable insights of electrochem. activation and carbon cathodes' electrochem. behaviors and will facilitate the construction of high-capacity carbon cathodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomQpg2Hf5ng7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgY4ZDsSQ8YKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXis1Oisr3P&amp;md5=2b4903fef03305ed4ec22dd0922d6d9d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.34133/2021/9857563"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sato, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoshikawa, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Integrating Bi@C Nanospheres in Porous Hard Carbon Frameworks for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Yazhan; Song, Ning; Zhang, Zhengchunyu; Chen, Weihua; Feng, Jinkui; Xi, Baojuan; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as an alternative technol. because of their merits in abundance and cost.  Realizing their real applications, however, remains a formidable challenge.  One is that among the limitations of anode materials, the alloy-type candidates tolerate fast capacity fading during cycling.  Here, a 3D framework superstructure assembled with carbon nanobelt arrays decorated with a metallic bismuth (Bi) nanospheres coated carbon layer by thermolysis of Bi-based metal-org. framework nanorods is synthesized as an anode material for SIBs.  Due to the unique structural superiority, the anode design promotes excellent sodium-storage performance in terms of high capacity, excellent cycling stability, and ultrahigh rate capability up to 80 A g-1 with a capacity of 308.8 mAh g-1.  The unprecedented sodium-storage ability is not only attributed to the unique hybrid architecture, but also to the prodn. of a homogeneous and thin solid electrolyte interface layer and the formation of uniform porous nanostructures during cycling in the ether-based electrolyte.  Importantly, deeper understanding of the underlying cause of the performance improvement is illuminated, which is vital to provide the theor. basis for application of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgzWKbs82Y-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgY4ZDsSQ8YKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhsVOgs77K&amp;md5=7222db8522f54e074fcc9c8d85c8a394</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.2c01202"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, B.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transgenic Engineering on Silicon Surfaces Enables Robust Interface Chemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jie; Yang, Zhen; Mao, Baoguang; Wang, Yixin; Jiang, Yan; Cao, Minhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Using electrolyte additives to manipulate the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) is an effective means to optimize battery performance; however, how to regulate their interactions with electrode surfaces, esp. for those relatively inert ones, is a huge challenge.  Here we demonstrate feasible transgenic engineering as a promising concept to address this challenge with Si anode as the platform.  MoSe2 is a better gene in comparison with the pristine Si for preferentially adsorbing and reducing the widely used electrolyte additive fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) to engineer the SEI, and based on this, we specifically constructed MoSe2-coated Si (Si@MoSe2).                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nature of Intrinsic Defects in Carbon Materials for Electrochemical Dechlorination of 1,2-Dichloroethane to Ethylene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Guoqiang; Fan, Shiying; Li, Xinyong; Wang, Jing; Bai, Chunpeng; Guo, Xuecheng; Tade, Moses; Liu, Shaomin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Catalysis</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">C materials were recognized as prospective catalysts for the electrocatalytic 1,2-dichloroethane (DCE) dechlorination reaction (DCEDR), which is an economical and environmentally friendly strategy for the control of DCE contamination and prodn. of highly valuable ethylene.  However, the precise nature of intrinsic defects (pentagon, heptagon, octagon, armchair edge, and zigzag edge) in C-based catalysts for the electrochem. DCEDR was not reported to date.  Herein, theor. calcns. demonstrated that pentagon site showed the lowest energy barrier of 0.12 eV, indicating a much higher electrochem. reactivity and ethylene selectivity of pentagon defect than those of others.  The prediction results were proved exptl. based on defective C materials with definitive defect configurations.  Therefore, intrinsic defects played a significant role in the electrocatalytic DCEDR and pentagon defect was responsible for the high performance of defective C catalysts.  This work not only clarifies the nature of intrinsic defects in C materials for electrochem. DCEDR but also provides the design principles for the rational prepn. of advanced C electrocatalysts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZ2Tsrgg2J7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgY4ZDsSQ8YKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXisVGrsb7M&amp;md5=fe9456413c365549e4b52bbe5a2f742f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1039/C4CS00499J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Skowron, S.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The presence of defects in graphene has an essential influence on its phys. and chem. properties.  The formation, behavior and healing of defects are detd. by energetic characteristics of at. scale structure changes.  In this article, we review recent studies devoted to at. scale reactions during thermally activated and irradn.-induced processes in graphene.  The formation energies of vacancies, adatoms and topol. defects are discussed.  Defect formation, healing and migration are quantified in terms of activation energies (barriers) for thermally activated processes and by threshold energies for processes occurring under electron irradn.  The energetics of defects in the graphene interior and at the edge is analyzed.  The effects of applied strain and a close proximity of the edge on the energetics of at. scale reactions are overviewed.  Particular attention is given to problems where further studies are required.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpv_trQ_xbHFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgY4ZDsSQ8YKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlt1Ciurc%253D&amp;md5=1f0d1888170a7e039145b34a0d4e2632</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2022.12.076"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, S.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2022.12.076</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D204%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D507-515%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DS.%2BJ.%2BDong%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BD.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BT.%2BWang%26author%3DF.%2BC.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BWu%26author%3DP.%2BC.%2BDai%26author%3DT.%2BXing%26author%3DX.%2BGu%26author%3DM.%2BB.%2BWu%26title%3DControllable%2BEngineering%2Bof%2BIntrinsic%2BDefects%2Bon%2BCarbon%2BNanosheets%2BEnables%2BFast%2Band%2BStable%2BPotassium%2BStorage%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2022.12.076&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2022.12.076&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable engineering of intrinsic defects on carbon nanosheets enables fast and stable potassium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Sijin; Li, Yang; Zhang, Mengdi; Wang, Juntao; Li, Fengchun; Wu, Shuang; Dai, Pengcheng; Xing, Tao; Gu, Xin; Wu, Mingbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">204</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">507-515</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Defect-enriched carbon nanomaterials possess high potassium storage capacity and rapid ion transport capability; nevertheless, their rate performance is restricted by the deteriorated electronic cond. induced by over-broken sp2-C conjugated structure.  Herein, intrinsic defect-enriched carbon nanosheet (DCS) with controllable defect d. is reported for the high-efficiency anode of potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  The DCS constructed by internal sp2-C configuration and external sp3-C defects can ensure good electron transport ability and afford abundant active sites for K+ storage.  As PIBs anode, DCS-24 obtained by ball-milling for 24 h with optimized defect d. delivers a high specific capacity of 270.9 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C, an excellent rate performance (189 mAh g-1 at 10 C), as well as long cycle durability (255.1 mAh g-1 over 3000 cycles at 1 C).  Electrochem. results and d. functional theory simulations indicate that the intrinsic defects of carbon materials improve the capacitive K+ storage capacity, speed up the K+ diffusion, and lower the K+ adsorption energy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpA7x-jmWYoubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5Rg3jrehCCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXnslKkuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=d84f7f376e2d5ea7a4b83bb385aaa7fc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202205933"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ling, L.                 10.1002/adma.202205933</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D34%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2205933%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26issue%3D42%26author%3DL.%2BL.%2BLing%26author%3DL.%2BJiao%26author%3DX.%2BS.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BDong%26author%3DW.%2BJ.%2BYang%26author%3DH.%2BJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DB.%2BJ.%2BYe%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DH.%2BL.%2BJiang%26title%3DPotassium-Assisted%2BFabrication%2Bof%2BIntrinsic%2BDefects%2Bin%2BPorous%2BCarbons%2Bfor%2BElectrocatalytic%2BCO2%2BReduction%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202205933&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202205933&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Potassium-assisted fabrication of intrinsic defects in porous carbons for electrocatalytic carbon dioxide reduction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ling, Li-Li; Jiao, Long; Liu, Xiaoshuo; Dong, Yun; Yang, Weijie; Zhang, Hongjun; Ye, Bangjiao; Chen, Jun; Jiang, Hai-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2205933</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The fabrication of intrinsic carbon defects is usually tangled with doping effects, and the identification of their unique roles in catalysis remains a tough task.  Herein, a K+-assisted synthetic strategy is developed to afford porous carbon (K-defect-C) with abundant intrinsic defects and complete elimination of heteroatom via direct pyrolysis of K+-confined metal-org. frameworks (MOFs).  Positron-annihilation lifetime spectroscopy, X-ray absorption fine structure measurement, and scanning transmission electron microscopy jointly illustrate the existence of abundant 12-vacancy-type carbon defects (V12) in K-defect-C.  Remarkably, the K-defect-C achieves ultrahigh CO Faradaic efficiency (99%) at -0.45 V in CO2 electroredn., far surpassing MOF-derived carbon without K+ etching.  Theor. calcns. reveal that the V12 defects in K-defect-C favor CO2 adsorption and significantly accelerate the formation of the rate-detg. COOH* intermediate, thereby promoting CO2 redn.  This work develops a novel strategy to generate intrinsic carbon defects and provides new insights into their crit. role in catalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGql9omIyi-OlrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5Rg3jrehCCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVagurvL&amp;md5=27e440695cb03b04683002c5d1f166ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.0c01808"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.
