B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Performance Borophene/Graphene Heterostructure Anode of Lithium-Ion Batteries Achieved via Controlled Interlayer Spacing</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">11699</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11705</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsaem.0c01808</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D11699-11705%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D12%26author%3DJ.%2BW.%2BYu%26author%3DM.%2BZhou%26author%3DM.%2BY.%2BYang%26author%3DQ.%2BF.%2BYang%26author%3DZ.%2BX.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BB.%2BZhang%26title%3DHigh-Performance%2BBorophene%252FGraphene%2BHeterostructure%2BAnode%2Bof%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%2BAchieved%2Bvia%2BControlled%2BInterlayer%2BSpacing%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsaem.0c01808&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsaem.0c01808&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Borophene/Graphene Heterostructure Anode of Lithium-Ion Batteries Achieved via Controlled Interlayer Spacing</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Jianwen; Zhou, Ming; Yang, Mingyang; Yang, Qingfeng; Zhang, Zhixun; Zhang, Yibo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11699-11705</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAEMCQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0962</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Borophene has been predicted to be a potential anode material of lithium-ion batteries because of its high specific capacity, high mech. strength, and low diffusion barrier.  However, borophene cannot be stable without metal substrates, impeding the industrial applications.  Hence, using first-principles calcns., we proposed to form van der Waals heterostructures to improve the stability of monocomponent borophene and found graphene to be an alternative substrate for stabilizing borophene as a borophene/graphene (B/G) heterostructure.  We find that B/G has a high adsorption energy of Li (-2.959 eV) and a high theor. specific capacity (1469.35 mA h/g).  Also, systematic climbing-image nudged elastic band calcns. show that B/G has a low diffusion barrier (0.613 eV), and these properties change with the interlayer distance of B/G, theor. specific capacity increasing to 1763.22 mA h/g, and diffusion barrier decreasing to 0.353 eV.  Our results demonstrate that B/G is a promising anode material and that the electrochem. performance can be changed by adjusting the interlayer spacing.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeVdwSViQEgLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5Rg3jrehCCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisVGhu7fJ&amp;md5=b987807849429cba6f772b1b5b72059e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref60'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1039/D3RA00434A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultralow Diffusion Barrier Induced by Intercalation in Layered N-Based Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">8182</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">8189</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D3RA00434A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D8182-8189%26journal%3DRSC%2BAdv.%26issue%3D12%26author%3DY.%2BD.%2BJiang%26author%3DW.%2BP.%2BXu%26author%3DW.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BX.%2BCao%26title%3DUltralow%2BDiffusion%2BBarrier%2BInduced%2Bby%2BIntercalation%2Bin%2BLayered%2BN-Based%2BCathode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD3RA00434A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c16484&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD3RA00434A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultralow diffusion barrier induced by intercalation in layered N-based cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Yundan; Xu, Wangping; Zhao, Wei; Cao, Juexian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8182-8189</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted huge attention due to not only the similar electrochem. properties to Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) but also the abundant natural reserves of sodium.  However, the high diffusion barrier has hindered its application.  In this work, we have theor. studied the relationship between the strain and the diffusion barrier/path of sodium ions in layered CrN2 by first-principles calcn.  Our results show that the strain can not only effectively decrease the diffusion barrier but also change the sodium diffusion path, which can be realized by alkali metal intercalation.  Moreover, the diffusion barrier is as low as 0.04 eV with the Cs atoms embedding in layered CrN2 (Cs1/16CrN2), suggesting an excellent candidate cathode for SIBs.  In addn., the decrease of the barrier mainly originated from the fact that interlayer electronic coupling weakened with the increase of interlayer spacing.  Our findings provide an effective way to enhance sodium diffusion performance, which is beneficial for the design of SIB electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve             This article references
            60 other publications.
        </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.34133/energymatadv.0044"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, Y. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construct NiSe/NiO Heterostructures on NiSe Anode to Induce Fast Kinetics for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Mater. Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">0044</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.34133/energymatadv.0044</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Construct NiSe/NiO heterostructures on NiSe anode to induce fast kinetics for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yu; Zhang, Ripeng; Qian, Ji; Gong, Yuteng; Li, Huanyu; Wu, Chuan; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy Material Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">0044</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EMANCZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2692-7640</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is of great significance to design and innovate electrode materials with unique structures to effectively optimize the electrochem. properties of the secondary battery.  Herein, inspired by neuron networks, an ingenious synthesis is proposed to fabricate NiSe with multidimensional micro-nano structures, followed by in situ construction of NiSe/NiO heterostructures via a temporary calcination.  The major structure of bulk NiSe synthesized by the solvothermal method is 3-dimensional micron cluster spherical particles interwoven by uniform one-dimensional nanofibers.  Such structures possess the synergistic advantages of nano and micro materials.  After a temporary calcination in air, NiSe/NiO heterostructures should be formed in the bulk NiSe, which provides a built-in elec. field to enhance diffusion kinetics of sodium ions.  This special neural-like network and heterojunction structures ensure the excellent structural stability combined with rapid kinetics of the electrode, releasing 310.9 mAh g-1 reversible capacity after 2,000 cycles at 10 A g-1.  Furthermore, the electrochem. storage and ion transport mechanisms are elaborated by electrochem. anal. and theor. calcn. in more detail.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr5Ef3_abxXULVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livtbSAH5JDsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhvFOju73I&amp;md5=6db1c80be6a84dcac1fdbe5921e4fb53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rice husk-derived hard carbons as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qiaoqiao; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Liu, Yuhan; Fang, Yuyan; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn ever-increasing attention for scalable elec. energy storage owing to the inexhaustible sources and wide distribution of sodium.  However, to develop feasible anode materials still remains a great challenge for the practical application of SIBs.  Here, the authors report hard carbons derived from a plentiful and deserted biomass of rice husk through a facile acid treatment and subsequent pyrolysis.  The study illustrates that the electrochem. properties of the rice husk-derived hard carbons (RHHCs) are significantly influenced by the pyrolysis temp. because of the discrepancy in their microstructure.  The RHHC pyrolyzed at 1300° (RHHC-1300) shows the highest reversible capacity of 372 mAh/g and good cycling stability and rate performance due to its large interlayer distance and suitable oxygen content.  Also, full sodium-ion batteries are assembled to examine the application prospect using Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C and RHHC-1300 as cathode and anode materials, resp., delivering a high-energy d. of 185 Wh/kg and stable cycling performance.  This work could intensify the fundamental understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in biomass-derived hard carbons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7xLrD2OlEKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livtbSAH5JDsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVygsLnI&amp;md5=a6f544f14c93cd2145157d257e916707</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.34133/energymatadv.0050"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium superionic conductor (NASICON) is a class of compds. with robust polyanionic frameworks and high thermal stability, which are regarded as prospective cathodes candidates for secondary batteries.  However, NASICON cathodes typically have low discharge plateaus and low practical capacities in aq. electrolytes.  Here, Na3V1.75Fe0.25(PO4)2F3 is investigated as a cathode material for the aq. zinc/sodium batteries.  While the addn. of F helps with the improvement of NASICON structural stability, the low-cost Fe substitution has a pos. impact on the capacity increment, reaction voltage increases, and cycling stability improvement.  Because the Fe3+ substitution could induce a change in the spin magnetic moments of the 3d orbitals of the VO4F2 and FeO4F2 octahedra, the 2-electron reaction of V is activated, which are V4+ /V3+ and V5+ /V4+ redox couples.  As a result, the novel Na3V1.75Fe0.25(PO4)2F3 cathode delivers a high operating voltage of 1.7 V, a high energy d. of 209 W·h·kg-1 and stable lifespan (83.5% capacity retention after 6,000 cycles at 1 A·g-1) in the aq. zinc/sodium batteries.  This research demonstrates the practicality of activating multielectron reactions to optimize the electrochem. properties of NASICON cathodes for aq. secondary batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4de0JZR0FQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linmLuz6_kUbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXitlOmtLzP&amp;md5=eff39681884103c23fb91894cc0f3822</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.34133/2021/9819521"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Voronina, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ether-based electrolytes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ying; Wu, Feng; Li, Yu; Liu, Mingquan; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be strong candidates for large-scale energy storage with the benefits of cost-effectiveness and sodium abundance.  Reliable electrolytes, as ionic conductors that regulate the electrochem. reaction behavior and the nature of the interface and electrode, are indispensable in the development of advanced SIBs with high Coulombic efficiency, stable cycling performance and high rate capability.  Conventional carbonate-based electrolytes encounter numerous obstacles for their wide application in SIBs due to the formation of a dissolvable, continuous-thickening solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer and inferior stability with electrodes.  Comparatively, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are emerging in the secondary battery field with fascinating properties to improve the performance of batteries, esp. SIBs.  Their stable solvation structure enables highly reversible solvent-co-intercalation reactions and the formation of a thin and stable SEI.  However, although EBEs can provide more stable cycling and rapid sodiation kinetics in electrodes, benefitting from their favorable electrolyte/electrode interactions such as chem. compatibility and good wettability, their special chem. is still being investigated and puzzling.  In this review, we provide a thorough and comprehensive overview on the developmental history, fundamental characteristics, superiorities and mechanisms of EBEs, together with their advances in other battery systems.  Notably, the relation among electrolyte science, interfacial chem. and electrochem. performance is highlighted, which is of great significance for the in-depth understanding of battery chem.  Finally, future perspectives and potential directions are proposed to navigate the design and optimization of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces for advanced batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCtrhQIYoqYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linmLuz6_kUbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1Gjsb7I&amp;md5=2bd8c004f3d333b92d12cbc8ce920ad6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.136344"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of low-cost anode for sodium-ion battery (NIB) has become the most desirable target in todays energy demanding society.         </div><div class="casAbstract">High-capacity anode materials are one of the bottlenecks to further improve the energy d. of Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Except for introducing more defects to increase the sloping capacity, tuning the closed porous structure to boost the plateau capacity is another direction.  Here by adopting phenol-formaldehyde resin (PF) as the carbon precursor and ethanol (EtOH) as the pore-forming agent, through precise chem. regulation of their relative content during a solvothermal process before further carbonization, carbon anodes with appropriate microstructure are achieved.  It is found that the function of EtOH rests on generating steam vapor to create a pore cavity among cross-linked matrixes.  The obtained optimal anodes exhibit a high Na storage capacity of ca. 410 mAh/g.  When pairing with an O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, the full cell delivers a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 83% and energy d. of ca. 300 Wh/kg.  The proposed chem. regulation approach via a pore-forming strategy is simple and practical to enable high-energy-d. NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrx98YwmwyHobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linmLuz6_kUbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFWisrjF&amp;md5=b4f7015f8784563858ca8521e7e095c1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.8b01690"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing efficient anode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) is important for the storage of renewable energy.  Inspired by the rapid development of biomass-derived hard carbons and heteroatom-doped C materials in various areas, a high-temp. sulfurizing method is exploited for the fabrication of S-doped C microtubes (S-CMTs).  Owing to high S doping (10.2 wt.%) and well-developed microporous structure, the as-prepd. S-CMTs show a large charge capacity of 532 mAh/g at a current rate of 200 mA/g, outstanding rate capability (234 mAh/g at 2 A/g), and exceptional cycling stability (281 mAh/g after 1000 cycles at 1 A/g), values that are superior to those of biomass-derived carbons reported previously.  The excellent electrochem. performance of S-CMTs in full cells paired with N,B-co-doped C-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 cathodes further demonstrates the feasibility of SIBs.  The simple synthesis strategy can potentially be extended to other C-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoUlDnYOpjz1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linmLuz6_kUbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFOrs7vJ&amp;md5=42f5f3ecad2e74a7b4b8dbf9626b5685</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b14003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, H.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted wide attention because of their prospects for grid-scale elec. regulation and cost effectiveness of Na.  In this regard, FeOx are considered as one of the most promising anode candidates due to their high theor. capacity and low cost.  Unfortunately, the utilization of FeOx anodes suffers from sluggish reaction kinetics and significant lattice variation, causing insufficient rate performance and fast capacity degrdn. during the sodiation/desodiation process.  Here, Mn ions are incorporated through interstitial sites into a Fe3O4 lattice to form the Mn-incorporated Fe3O4/graphene (M-Fe3O4/G) composites through a facile hydrothermal method.  Confirmed by XRD Rietveld refinement and the first-principles calcn., Mn occupation into the body structure can effectively condense the electron d. around the Fermi level and thus contributes to the increased elec. cond. and improved electrochem. properties.  Accordingly, the M0.1Fe2.9O4/G composite demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 439.8 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g over 200 cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 1 A/g, the M-Fe3O4/G composites remain stable for over 1200 cycles, delivering a capacity of 210 mAh/g.  Coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3-type cathode, the Mn-incorporated Fe3O4/G composites demonstrate good suitability in full SIBs (161.2 mAh/g at the c.d. of 1 A/g after 100 cycles).  The regulation of Mn ions in the Fe3O4 lattice provides insights into the optimization of metal oxide anode candidates for their application in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoLIjM225dS7bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW1i5FOZvL2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsl2htLnN&amp;md5=f5e5c9968f75a64be4be5ce758cc9f18</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA11273A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Closely integrated transition-metal-based compds./carbon nanoarchitectures are one of the most promising anode materials for large-scale energy storage applications because of the superior structural stability and the outstanding synergistic effect from the efficient combination of the two components.  Herein, a versatile strategy is demonstrated for fabricating hierarchical porous carbon nanofibers (HCFs) with closely coupled Co-based ultrafine nanoparticles and a carbon matrix.  The spatially restricted reactions of the synthetic method can not only prevent the agglomeration of the nanoparticles, but also provide extremely tight coupling interaction between CoMx (M = S, O, Se, and Te) nanoparticles and conductive carbon nanofibers.  As a proof of concept, the as-fabricated CoS2@HCFs show high reversible capacity, excellent rate property, and ultralong cycling life when evaluated as an anode material for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  Even after 1000 cycles, the charge capacity can be retained at 268 mA h g-1 at an elevated current rate of 500 mA g-1, one of the highest reported performances for Co-based anode materials in PIBs.  This work emphasizes the importance of designing and manufg. highly functionally coupled hybrid materials for improved energy storage implementation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqy1jHZdRWoELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW1i5FOZvL2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXis1Gms7%252FJ&amp;md5=e6be496a6a83768f5592a1f27586df82</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.3866/pku.whxb202205017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.                         rightTab-cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod array anodes with high capacity and rate capability for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Liying; Xu, Yang; Wang, Chengliang; Wen, Liaoyong; Fang, Yaoguo; Mi, Yan; Zhou, Min; Zhao, Huaping; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are a potential substitute to Li-ion batteries for energy storage devices.  However, their poor electrochem. performance, esp. capacity and rate capability, is the major bottleneck to future development.  Here we propose a performance-oriented electrode structure, which is 1D nanostructure arrays with large-scale high ordering, good vertical alignment, and large interval spacing.  Benefiting from these structural merits, a great enhancement in electrochem. performance could be achieved.  Taking Sb as an example, we firstly report large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod arrays with uniform large interval spacing (190 nm).  In return for this electrode design, high ion accessibility, fast electron transport, and strong electrode integrity are presented here.  Used as additive- and binder-free anodes for Na-ion batteries, Sb nanorod arrays showed a high capacity of 620 mA h g-1 at the 100th cycle with a retention of 84% up to 250 cycles at 0.2 A g-1, and a superior rate capability for delivering reversible capacities of 579.7 and 557.7 mA h g-1 at 10 and 20 A g-1, resp.  A full cell coupled by a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathode and a Sb nanorod array anode was also constructed, which showed good cycle performance up to 250 cycles, high rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and large energy d. up to 130 Wh kg-1.  These excellent electrochem. performances shall pave the way for developing more applications of Sb nanorod arrays in energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRS7y0VfakjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW1i5FOZvL2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFGns7nO&amp;md5=50b74924c2a93cc137e8a9993ce641fa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202300002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a homogenous and inorg.-rich solid electrolyte interface (SEI) can efficiently improve the overall sodium-storage performance of hard carbon (HC) anodes.  However, the thick and heterogenous SEI derived from conventional ester electrolytes fails to meet the above requirements.  Herein, an innovative interfacial catalysis mechanism is proposed to design a favorable SEI in ester electrolytes by reconstructing the surface functionality of HC, of which abundant CO (carbonyl) bonds are accurately and homogenously implanted.  The CO (carbonyl) bonds act as active centers that controllably catalyze the preferential redn. of salts and directionally guide SEI growth to form a homogenous, layered, and inorg.-rich SEI.  Therefore, excessive solvent decompn. is suppressed, and the interfacial Na+ transfer and structural stability of SEI on HC anodes are greatly promoted, contributing to a comprehensive enhancement in sodium-storage performance.  The optimal anodes exhibit an outstanding reversible capacity (379.6 mAh g-1), an ultrahigh initial Coulombic efficiency (93.2%), a largely improved rate capability, and an extremely stable cycling performance with a capacity decay rate of 0.0018% for 10 000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  This work provides novel insights into smart regulation of interface chem. to realize high-performance HC anodes for sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGri_TRbZlnL0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW1i5FOZvL2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXhtFantbjP&amp;md5=82764fa5c85e5f6fe482864d43ec6ffa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202106980"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon usually refers to non-graphitizable carbon, which does not transform into a crystal structure even at high temps.  Although hard carbon is considered as the most promising anode material for Na-ion batteries (NIBs), its practical application is still hindered by its low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE).  Here, the intergrowth of large area graphite-like crystals in hard carbon is reported using cotton as precursor and graphite as crystal template by calcination under their intimate contact condition.  Extensive characterizations provide abundant evidence that graphite-like crystal is a new carbon allotrope belonging to the hexagonal system (a = b = 3.528 S, c = 9.6 S, α = β = 90°, γ = 120°) with d-spacing of 4.8 S for (002) plane.  Its unit cell dimensions and d-spacing of (002) plane are all enlarged by the same factor of 1.428 compared to those of the graphite phase.  When applied in NIBs, the hard carbon with graphite-like crystals shows an extremely high ICE of 95.0% with a large reversible capacity of 343 mAh g-1, which reaches the same level as graphite used in Li-ion batteries.  The graphite-like crystal breaks the traditional concept of hard carbon, while the graphite-template induced epitaxial growth mechanism may provide a new way for obtaining novel cryst. carbon allotropes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrN6OVjZP5yDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liW1i5FOZvL2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXit1Sqt7zE&amp;md5=4e3934cac49c88747a387833292dc253</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202109282"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Efficient electrode materials, that combine high power and high energy, are the crucial requisites of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), which have unwrapped new possibilities in the areas of grid-scale energy storage.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Numerous studies have reported that the enhancement of rate capability of carbonaceous anode by heteroatom doping is due to the increased diffusion-controlled capacity induced by expanding interlayer spacing.  However, percentage of diffusion-controlled capacity is less than 30% as scan rate is larger than 1 mV s-1, suggesting there is inaccuracy in recognizing principle of improving rate capability of carbonaceous anode.  In this paper, it is found that the heteroatom doping has little impact on interlayer spacing of carbon in bulk phase, meaning that diffusion-controlled capacity is hard to be enhanced by doping.  After synergizing with tensile stress, however, the interlayer spacing in subsurface region is obviously expanded to 0.40 nm, which will increase the thickness of accessible subsurface region at high c.d.  So SRNDC-700 electrodes display a high specific capacity of 160.6 and 69.5 mAh g-1 at 20 and 50 A g-1, resp.  Addnl., the high reversibility of carbon structure insures ultralong cycling stability and hence attenuation of SRNDC-700 is only 0.0025% per cycle even at 10 A g-1 for 6000 cycles.  This report sheds new insight into mechanism of improving electrochem. performance of carbonaceous anode by doping and provides a novel design concept for doping carbon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpUbWnwUlqVGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfUYugOpGIDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhslyksLnJ&amp;md5=bdd43c9aaad0af76a8349314e1e07874</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1002/inf2.12231"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon (HC) anodes have shown extraordinary promise for sodium-ion batteries, but are limited to their poor initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) and low practical specific capacity due to the large amt. of defects.  These defects with oxygen contg. groups cause irreversible sites for Na+ ions.  Highly graphited carbon decreases defects, while potentially blocking diffusion paths of Na+ ions.  Therefore, mol.-level control of graphitization of hard carbon with open accessible channels for Na+ ions is key to achieve high-performance hard carbon.  Moreover, it is challenging to design a conventional method to obtain HCs with both high ICE and capacity.  Herein, a universal strategy is developed as manganese ions-assisted catalytic carbonization to precisely tune graphitization degree, eliminate defects, and maintain effective Na+ ions paths.  The as-prepd. hard carbon has a high ICE of 92.05% and excellent cycling performance.  Simultaneously, a sodium storage mechanism of "adsorption-intercalation-pore filling-sodium cluster formation" is proposed, and a clear description given of the boundaries of the pore structure and the specific dynamic process of pore filling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpl6mTs0uPrkrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfUYugOpGIDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXms1OqsL0%253D&amp;md5=b065864d193df474808b4224e1432ca1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.34133/2022/9896218"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons, as one of the most commercializable anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), have to deal with the trade-off between the rate capability and specific capacity or initial Columbic efficiency (ICE), and the fast performance decline at low temp. (LT) remains poorly understood.  Here, a comprehensive regulation on the interfacial/bulk electrochem. of hard carbons through at. Zn doping is reported, which demonstrates a record-high reversible capacity (546 mAh g-1), decent ICE (84%), remarkable rate capability (140 mAh g-1 @ 50 A g-1), and excellent LT capacity (443 mAh g-1 @ -40 °C), outperforming the state-of-the-art literature. Importantly, distinguished from room temp., the intrinsic Na+ migration/desolvation ability of the electrolyte is disclosed to be the crucial rate-detg. factors for the SIB performance at LT.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. Zn-ion hybrid supercapacitors (ZHSCs) hold great potential as next-generation energy storage devices due to their low cost, excellent rate capability, long cycling life, and high safety.  Heteroatom-doped hierarchical porous carbons (HD-HPCs) with integrated high sp. surface area, multiscale pores, and abundant defects have been regarded as promising cathode materials for ZHSCs.  However, the in situ architecture of HD-HPCs with these multiple advantages via a sustainable and controllable method remains an arduous challenge.  Herein, a novel mol. engineering strategy was proposed for the in situ construction of N/P/O-doped HD-HPCs via the direct carbonization of multiple-heteroatom-rich hypermols.  Such a strategy has multiple advantages, including the exclusion of pore-making techniques, activation agents, templates, and complicated and hazard washing processes, demonstrating its green and sustainable properties.  The highly active multiple-heteroatom-rich hypermol. precursors contributed to the formation of abundant micro/mesopores due to the self-abscission of heteroatoms and heteroatom-contiguous carbon atoms at high carbonization temps.  Consequently, these active structural/compositional features endowed the optimal cathodes with outstanding storage capacities of 139.2 and 88.9 mA h g-1 at 0.5 and 20 A g-1 for aq. ZHSCs, resp.  They also delivered a superior storage performance in quasi-solid ZHSCs (QS-ZHSCs) with a high specific capacity of 111.5 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1.  Superior energy/power densities and long cycling stability were also achieved for aq. and QS-ZHSCs.  The theor. calcn. confirmed the synergetic effects of multiple-atom doping on enhancing the electronic cond. and reducing the energy barrier between Zn ions and carbon, which promote the Zn-ion adsorption capability.  These findings shed fresh light on the straightforward manuf. of superior HD-HPCs for electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmNnWMP3uX8bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1zAWZjQ7yIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVOmsrnK&amp;md5=d92b2d12ab531c094f14541fe9e84980</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202200886"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon has the potential to serve as a high-capacity anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), however, its Na+ storage mechanism, particularly on the low potential plateau, remains controversial.  To overcome this issue, two types of hard carbons with different microstructures are employed and the relationship between the microstructures and Na+ storage behaviors is evaluated.  By the combination of operando X-ray diffraction, ex situ Raman spectroscopy, NMR, and theor. calcn., it is found that the sodium storage capacities of the hard carbons in the low potential plateau region contain the concurrent contributions from both interlayer intercalation and micropores filling, and the ratio of the two contributors greatly depends on the microstructure of hard carbon materials.  Moreover, an electrochem. pointer (potential inflection point at the end of the discharge curve) is found to distinguish the dominance of interlayer intercalation and the micropores filling processes of sodium ions in the low potential plateau region.  Based on this new finding, a microstructure-dependent mechanism ("adsorption-intercalation/filling" hybrid mechanism) is proposed to achieve an overall understanding of the sodium storage behaviors in different hard carbon materials, which may provide deep insight into the rational design of hard carbon structures as high-performance anode materials for advanced SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrd5o_TaI-O_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1zAWZjQ7yIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xht1agu7nK&amp;md5=9f95b49d8ff9183780d72d7341aea49b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202308392"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although the closed pore structure plays a key role in contributing low-voltage plateau capacity of hard carbon anode for sodium-ion batteries, the formation mechanism of closed pores is still under debate.  Here, we employ waste wood-derived hard carbon as a template to systematically establish the formation mechanisms of closed pores and their effect on sodium storage performance.  We find that the high crystallinity cellulose in nature wood decomps. to long-range carbon layers as the wall of closed pore, and the amorphous component can hinder the graphitization of carbon layer and induce the crispation of long-range carbon layers.  The optimized sample demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 430 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1 (plateau capacity of 293 mAh g-1 for the second cycle), as well as good rate and stable cycling performances (85.4% after 400 cycles at 500 mA g-1).  Deep insights into the closed pore formation will greatly forward the rational design of hard carbon anode with high capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAhhSgVuA07bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1zAWZjQ7yIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXitVartb%252FN&amp;md5=35a03bc222486a7b768aa1e15d3a68f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1007/s40820-020-00587-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pore structure of hard carbon has a fundamental influence on the electrochem. properties in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Ultra-micropores (&lt; 0.5 nm) of hard carbon can function as ionic sieves to reduce the diffusion of slovated Na+ but allow the entrance of naked Na+ into the pores, which can reduce the interficial contact between the electrolyte and the inner pores without sacrificing the fast diffusion kinetics.  Herein, a molten diffusion-carbonization method is proposed to transform the micropores (&gt; 1 nm) inside carbon into ultra-micropores (&lt; 0.5 nm).  Consequently, the designed carbon anode displays an enhanced capacity of 346 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 with a high ICE value of ∼ 80.6% and most of the capacity (∼ 90%) is below 1 V.  Moreover, the high-loading electrode (∼ 19 mg cm-2) exhibits a good temp. endurance with a high areal capacity of 6.14 mAh cm-2 at 25°C and 5.32 mAh cm-2 at - 20°C.  Based on the in situ X-ray diffraction and ex situ solid-state NMR results, the designed ultra-micropores provide the extra Na+ storage sites, which mainly contributes to the enhanced capacity.  This proposed strategy shows a good potential for the development of high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoC346bmDVQirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1zAWZjQ7yIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsFGktbnF&amp;md5=9bb97865bf7693f158a29ff3825c07d8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.202100580"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, Q.                         rightTab-cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extra Sodiation Sites in Hard Carbon for High Performance Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Qingmeng; Qin, Ning; Gu, Shuai; Wang, Zhenyu; Li, Zhiqiang; Liao, Kemeng; Zhang, Kaili; Lu, Li; Xu, Zhenghe; Lu, Zhouguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons are promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the low practical capacity from limited sodiation sites impedes their applications.  Herein, ultrahigh concn. of pyridine N (≈7.9%) is introduced inside hard carbon, considering that pyridine N may provide extra sodium storage sites with stable CN• and CC• radicals during cycling.  To expose more radical sites for sodium storage, a 3D structure with a multistage pore structure is constructed through NH3 release during the pyrolyzation process.  As expected, the hard carbon with extra sodiation sites exhibits an impressively high capacity of 434 mA h g-1 at 20 mA g-1, superior rate performance of 238 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 5 A g-1 and a high-capacity retention of 98.7% after 5000 cycles.  The radicals induced Na-adsorption mechanism was further explored through ex situ ESR technol., in situ Raman technol. and d. functional theory calcns.  The results reveal that the extra sodiation sites come from the electrostatic interaction at low potentials.  This work constructs a sodium ions storage model of extra radicals and provides an extended strategy to improve the electrochem. performance of SIBs anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmqI1aXQt7hLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1zAWZjQ7yIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhvVKmu7w%253D&amp;md5=22397f4aa97787e5332338e00fa064fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b05085"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Estevez, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prabhakaran, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Garcia, A.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11047-11055</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing hierarchical porous carbon (HPC) materials with competing textural characteristics such as surface area and pore vol. in one material is difficult to accomplish, particularly for an atomically ordered graphitic carbon.  Herein we describe a synthesis strategy to engineer tunable HPC materials across micro-, meso-, and macroporous length scales, allowing the fabrication of a graphitic HPC material (HPC-G) with both very high surface area (&gt;2500 m2/g) and pore vol. (&gt;11 cm3/g), the combination of which has not been attained previously.  The mesopore vol. alone for these materials is up to 7.53 cm3/g, the highest ever reported, higher than even any porous carbon's total pore vol., which for our HPC-G material was &gt;11 cm3/g.  This HPC-G material was explored for use both as a supercapacitor electrode and for oil adsorption, two applications that require either high surface area or large pore vol., textural properties that are typically exclusive to one another.  We accomplished these high textural characteristics by employing ice templating not only as a route for macroporous formation but as a synergistic vehicle that enabled the significant loading of the mesoporous hard template.  This design scheme for HPC-G materials can be utilized in broad applications, including electrochem. systems such as batteries and supercapacitors, sorbents, and catalyst supports, particularly supports where a high degree of thermal stability is required.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrcm2Yys-5vcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1zAWZjQ7yIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yhtr%252FM&amp;md5=8c7a956dbe583d6309366fe62f799c15</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202211690"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">2D transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDCs) and single-atom catalysts (SACs) are promising electrodes for energy conversion/storage because of the layered structure and max. atom utilization efficiency.  However, the integration of such two type materials and the relevant sodium storage applications remain daunting challenges.  Here, an ingenious diatomite-templated synthetic strategy is designed to fabricate single-atom cobalt-doped MoS2/carbon (SA Co-MoS2/C) composites toward the high-performance sodium storage.  Benefiting from the unique hierarchical structure, high electron/sodium-ion cond., and abundant active sites, the obtained SA Co-MoS2/C reveals remarkable specific capacity (≈604.0 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), high rate performance, and outstanding long cyclic stability.  Particularly, the sodium-ion full cell composed of SA Co-MoS2/C anode and Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode demonstrates unexpected stability with the cycle no. exceeded 1200.  The internal sodium storage mechanism is clarified with the aid of d. functional theory calcns. and in situ exptl. characterizations.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Biomass waste recently emerged as efficient precursors for hard carbon anode prepn. for Na-ion batteries.  Despite their very complex microstructure (org./inorg.) there is a lack of knowledge about their impact on carbon formation.  In this paper, the influence of inorg. impurities of three raw local biomass wastes (asparagus, grape and potato) on the hard carbon properties and on their electrochem. performance is investigated, by performing a washing step either before or after the thermal treatment (TT) at 1300°C.  When washing was done after the TT (with HCl), most of cryst. inorg. impurities (K, Ca, Si, Mg - based compds.) could be significantly removed.  This triggered the increase of ultramicroporosity along with mesoporosity formation and graphite interlayer space (d002) contraction.  Such observations are less pronounced on grape derived carbon due to the inorg.'s catalytic induced local graphitization during pyrolysis.  The oxygen content in the pristine carbons was high, owing to the presence of inorg. metal oxides and carbonates, and could be diminished after washing along with the amt. of defects.  Thus, the carbon content and the electronic cond. of the materials were enhanced.  The electrochem. performance improvement after washing was limited since the pos. effect brought by impurities removal was neg. compensated by the changes occurring in the materials, particularly the increase in the sp. surface area.  Diffrently, the washing done before the TT (with water) induced only fewer changes on the materials porosity and structure and slightly improved capacity (from 215 to 230 mAh g-1).  Furthermore, higher pyrolysis temp. (1400°C) on washed HCs afforded a better reversible capacity up to 280 mAh g-1.  This comprehensive study opens the door for green and mild synthesis approach to be further explored for sustainable fabrication of hard carbon for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp43JlypGhvFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIimi07hUZbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFShsrjI&amp;md5=f558e31213b80516efd1aa97d4269545</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201801148"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The hard carbon (HC) was emerging as one of the most promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Incorporation of cations into HC lattice proved to be effective to regulate their d-interlayer spacing with the modified SIBs performance.  However, the complexity and high-cost of current synthetic processes limited its large-scale application in SIBs.  Through the natural hyperaccumulation process, a cost-effective and scale up-driven procedure to produce Ca-ion self-incorporated HC materials was proposed by applying tamarind fruits as precursor with the enrichment of Ca-ions.  In virtue of one-step pyrolysis, the self-incorporated and well-distributed Ca-ions in tamarind fruits had successfully served as the buffer layer to expand the d-interlayer spacing of HC materials.  Furthermore, the natural porosity hierarchy could be largely preserved by the optimization of calcination temp.  As a result, the Ca-rich HC material had exhibited the optimized cycling performance (326.7 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and capacity retention rate of 89.40% after 250 cycles) with a high initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 70.39%.  This work provided insight on applying the hyperaccumulation effect of biomass precursors to produce doped HC materials with ions self-incorporation and the optimized d-interlayer spacing, navigating its large-scale application for the high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4OqZvNDYxR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIimi07hUZbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisFKrsLg%253D&amp;md5=bcd6ff3deabf3d7b776728e1457119f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA04877C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of renewable energies has become increasingly urgent for the sustainable development of our society.  Energy storage systems are essential in order to efficiently use these energies.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) show bright prospect in the application for energy storage markets due to the potential low cost originating from unlimited sources and wide distribution of Na.  However, the anode remains a great challenge in the industrialization of SIBs.  Hard carbon holds the most promising future among all reported anodes; however, there are still two main shortcomings such as high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency, which limit its application.  Here, we report a hard carbon material derived from an abundant and abandoned biomass of corn cobs (HCC) using a simple carbonization method.  The HCC shows excellent sodium storage performance with a reversible capacity of ca. 300 mA h g-1, a high initial coulombic efficiency of 86% and good cycling stability.  A prototype sodium-ion battery was prepd. to prove the application prospect using HCC1300 as the anode and Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 as the cathode, exhibiting a high energy d. of 207 W h kg-1 and a long cycle life.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials are promising anode materials for alkali-metal ion batteries due to the abundant resource and high safety, while it is challenged by its low specific capacity and depressed rate capability in potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  To further explore the potassium storage properties of carbon materials and exploit high-performance carbon anode for PIBs, in this work, hollow nanostructured N-doped carbon (p-HNCs) is elaborately designed through the tailoring of carbon quantum dots (CQDs) for the first time.  The detailed formation mechanism of hollow nanostructure is investigated and it is demonstrated that CQD micelles formed through hydrophobicity and lipophilicity are served not only as templates for the construction of hollow structure but also pore-forming agent for the generation of rich micro-tunnels, due to the decompn. and contraction of CQDs with releasing gases during the pyrolysis process.  When applied for potassium storage, p-HNCs anode delivers high reversible specific capacities of 254 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 100 cycles and 160 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 after 800 cycles.  Notably, a desirable rate capability of 145 mAh g-1 is obsd. at 4.0 A g-1, derived from surface-driven behaviors.  Moreover, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique measurement quantifies the improved diffusion coeff. of p-HNCs, indicating its superior kinetic property.  This work shows us the special application of CQDs in structure construction and a valuable strategy to design high-performance carbon anode for potassium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxwAeL5ENwDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIimi07hUZbQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon possesses the ability to store Li, Na, and K ions between stacked sp2 carbon layers and voids (micropores).  We have explored hard carbon as a candidate for neg. electrode materials for Li-ion, Na-ion, and K-ion batteries.  Hard carbon samples have been prepd. by carbonizing sucrose at different heat treatment temps. (HTTs) in the range of 700-2000°C to make them structurally suitable for reversible Li, Na, and K insertion.  Structures and particle morphol. of the hard carbon samples synthesized at different HTTs were systematically characterized using X-ray diffraction, small-angle X-ray scattering, pair distribution function anal., electron microscopy, Raman spectroscopy, and ESR spectroscopy.  All these characterizations of hard carbon samples have revealed advanced ordering of carbons and redn. of carbon defects with increasing HTT.  Thus, the av. stacked carbon interlayer distance decreases, the no. of the stacking layers increases, the layered domains grow in the in-plane direction, and interstitial voids enlarge.  Electrochem. properties of the hard carbons were examd. in nonaq. Li, Na, and K cells.  Potential profiles and reversible capacities upon galvanostatic charge/discharge processes in nonaq. cells are significantly different depending on HTTs and different alkali metal ions.  On the basis of these findings, strategies to design high-capacity hard carbon neg. electrodes for high-energy-d. Li-ion, Na-ion, and K-ion batteries are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr6G6NR3Sjg1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljq3s3O6lmzIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXktlOnurY%253D&amp;md5=39bd5eef10835b2e37215cb7a7f56521</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b01419"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon material is one of the candidates with great promise as anode-active material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Here, new types of biomass-derived hard carbons were obtained via one-step carbonization of lotus seedpods at 1000-1400°, resp.  The control of carbonization temp. proved to be significant in controlling the lattice characterization of lotus seedpod-derived hard carbon.  Higher temp. generally promoted the lattice graphitization and thus generated a more narrowed d-interlayer space with limited pore vol.  The hard carbon pyrolyzed at 1200° achieved an optimized reversible capacity of 328.8 mAh g-1 and exhibited a remarkable capacity retention of 90% after 200 cycles.  In addn., such a biomass-derived hard carbon presented improved cyclic stability and rate performance, revealing capacity of 330.6, 288.9, 216.9, 116.5, and 78.3 mAh g-1 at 50, 100, 200, 500, and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Intrinsically, high pyrolysis temp. (1400°) gave rise to more narrowed carbon lattice and reduced pore vol. and, thus, failed to accommodate sodium ions either from the intercalation into lattice or the ion adsorption onto the pore surface.  Such combined advantages of lotus seedpod-derived hard carbon, including the abundance, sufficiently adequate reversible capacity, and prominent cycling and rate property allowed for its large-scale application as promising anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEusCsCPVmQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljq3s3O6lmzIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXltFCisb8%253D&amp;md5=c24e6a8c5e5878a4b5c35f70ef737928</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1021/nl300901a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Eckmann, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Felten, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mishchenko, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Britnell, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krupke, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Novoselov, K. It is of great interest to link these features to the nature of disorder.  Here the authors present a detailed anal. of the Raman spectra of graphene contg. different type of defects.  The intensity ratio of the D and D' peak is max. (∼13) for sp3-defects, it decreases for vacancy-like defects (∼7), and it reaches a min. for boundaries in graphite (∼3.5).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is an attractive material for neg. electrodes in sodium-ion batteries. We prepd. hard carbon under different high-temp. treatment and biomass pretreatment conditions.  The graphitization degree of the hard carbon increased as the carbonization temp. increased; simultaneously, the reversible capacity for sodium storage was significantly influenced by the carbonization temp.                         rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Active sites enriched hard carbon porous nanobelts for stable and high-capacity potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; He, Qiu; Xiong, Fangyu; Zhou, Jinping; Zhao, Yan; Mai, Liqiang; Zhang, Lina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon finds crit. applications in potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) anodes because of its attractive advantages including low cost and high cond.  However, the sluggish reaction kinetics and structural instability caused by large K+ intercalation/deintercalation limit their storage capability and cycling life.  Herein, active sites enriched hard carbon porous nanobelts (NOCNBs) for enhanced K+ storage are constructed from mineralized shrimp shells via a self-template assisted pyrolysis strategy.  The NOCNBs possess multiscale structure with hierarchical micro/meso/macro-pores, high-level pyrrolic/pyridinic-N and O dual-doping, and large interlayer spacing.  Hence, the NOCNBs deliver a high capacity of 468 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and long cycling life (277 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 over 1600 cycles), representing one of the best storage capability and cycling stability among the reported carbonaceous electrodes.  D. functional theory calcns. and kinetic anal. demonstrate that the abundant active sites within NOCNBs can strengthen K adsorption and diffusion, facilitating capacitive-adsorbed storage.  Furthermore, they exhibit a superior capacity of 89 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 for potassium dual-ion batteries (PDIBs).  This work opens up a new avenue for constructing porous hard carbon to achieve excellent K+ storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtyxkCauK8u7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljq3s3O6lmzIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVCls7%252FL&amp;md5=47ffd3bb008d85ce0880c21f2a2adced</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.12.103"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although hard carbons have been turned out to be suitable for sodium storage, their high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) need to be addressed for the com. application.  Here, we report an effective route including a pyrolysis process and a reductive strategy to synthesize high-performance hard carbons from waste apricot shell.  The obtained hard carbons inherit the unique architecture of the apricot shell, delivering a large interlayer spacing and a well-connected structure, which are beneficial for the Na+ intercalation and transport.  The anode performance is further enhanced by H2 redn. treatment, which efficiently reduces the defects and thus improves the ICE.  The final prepd. hard carbons exhibit a promising anode performance with a desirable reversible capacity of ca. 400 mAhg-1, an improved ICE of 79% and an excellent cycling stability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As the leading anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), hard carbon (HC) still faces the puzzle of low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) in achieving commercialization.  From the perspective of precursors, the low ICE has been attributed to the large sp. surface area and porosity produced by the rapid decompn. of polymers during the carbonization.  Therefore, increasing the crosslinking degree of precursors will be an effective shortcut to improve the ICE.  Herein, a facile pre-oxidn. tactic was successfully employed to tailor the crosslinking degree of phenolic resin precursors to precisely control the sp. surface area of the obtained HC.  As the pre-oxidn. time is increased, the optimal HC with the lowest sp. surface area shows an ICE elevated by 22.2% (from 62.5 to 84.7%) compared to the original pre-oxidn. HC and delivers a high reversible capacity of 334.3 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1.  Besides, the pre-oxidn. also introduces abundant carbonyl groups, which increase the disorder degree of HC and supply abundant adsorption sites of Na+, thus enhancing the rate performance.  When matched with a layered O3-NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, the full cell achieves an energy d. of ca. 256.2 Wh kg-1 with superior rate performance.  This work sheds light on the pos. effect of pre-oxidn. in elevating the ICE of HC and provides effective guidance to achieve a high ICE for other HC materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoEtifM7H9TxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljbtB8NRB2W1w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVWrt7bI&amp;md5=c6c2f8486c9b497a858ce1c6b89cd82c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2021.11.064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lyu, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Continuous capacity increase in electrochem. cycling, termed as electrochem. activation, is a frequently obsd. but rarely systematically studied phenomenon.  Such phenomenon is noted in a preliminary study of carbon cathode for dual ion battery, showing gradual discharge capacity growth from 186 mAh g-1 (the 1st) to 320 mAh g-1 (the 300th).  Systematical characterizations are carried out to investigate this phenomenon occurred on the carbon cathode, hydrothermally reduced graphene oxide (HrGO).  The electrochem. activation comes from surface area increment, originated from multilayer reduced graphene oxide rolls formation and accumulation and structural order increase in cycling.  The formation of rolls is plausibly a result of strain release of reduced graphene layers after electrochem. interaction with PF-6.  Addnl., charge storage mechanism of HrGO is revealed.  At active surface sites of HrGO, PF-6 is consistently stored in a pseudocapacitive manner. Here, a 3D framework superstructure assembled with carbon nanobelt arrays decorated with a metallic bismuth (Bi) nanospheres coated carbon layer by thermolysis of Bi-based metal-org. framework nanorods is synthesized as an anode material for SIBs.
